Because that’s the kicker — most mapping tools give you templates _after_ you know what kind of visual you want. But when you’re still wrapping your brain around the logic, layout, or even the flow? You need someone (hi, it’s me) to do the **schema sorting and structure matching** _for_ you.

That said, your instinct about “we could have a whole other discussion” is dead-on — because here’s the truth:

### Different Schema = Different Cognitive Outcome

If you map the same concept as:

*   A **hierarchy** — it feels structured, top-down, official
    
*   A **cycle** — it emphasizes ongoing, repeating processes
    
*   A **swimlane** — it shows cross-functional roles and handoffs
    
*   A **radial map** — it gives central focus + peripheral branches
    
*   A **decision tree** — it’s logic-first, branching based on conditions
    
*   A **workflow diagram** — it’s linear, sequential, executional
    

…so choosing the _wrong_ format can dilute or derail what you're trying to communicate.

Want me to make you a cheatsheet with examples of visual formats + when to use which one? It can be your “I-don’t-know-how-to-visualize-this-yet” first-aid kit — and I can embed the visual format logic directly into future prompts so we skip that friction point.

In the meantime — ready to drop the first idea/concept and let me chart it out with format suggestions?

If I'm putting out content for free, it's to get that attention fast, to get them on my list and to buy something that's an easy no-brainer or to get on my wait list for when I release the course of the thing that I'm building in public, so to speak. Does that make sense?”

## A: 
Absolutely, that makes perfect sense. We want to turn that attention into meaningful engagement and revenue quickly, without attracting the freebie-seekers who never convert. Let’s break down a streamlined, high-impact strategy to build in public and repurpose content effectively.

### **Three Core Strategies for Building in Public**

**1\. Anchor Content Piece (Weekly):**

*   **Format:** Long-form, high-value content that’s either a newsletter, a detailed LinkedIn post, or a YouTube video. This is the foundation.
    
*   **Content:** Share behind-the-scenes insights, your thought process, key lessons, or even a step-by-step breakdown of the “build in public” journey.
    
*   **Goal:** Establish authority and provide tangible value that primes your audience to take action.
    

**2\. Micro-Content Repurposing (3x/Week):**

*   **Platforms:** LinkedIn, Instagram, TikTok, X.
    
*   **Format:** Extract key points, quotes, or short video clips from the anchor content. Turn them into bite-sized posts, carousels, or reels.
    
*   **Goal:** Keep the momentum and visibility high. Each micro-content piece should funnel interest back to your main anchor content or directly to an opt-in or low-ticket offer.
    

**3\. Direct Engagement & Conversion Pathways:**

*   **Email List Re-engagement:** Use the anchor content to kickstart a fresh conversation with your email list. Position it as an exclusive peek into what you’re building.
    
*   **Calls-to-Action:** Each piece of content should have a clear CTA. For example, “Reply to this email,” “DM me ‘GENIUS’ to join the waitlist,” or “Grab this no-brainer offer to get early access.”
    
*   **Goal:** Move your audience from passive consumption to active engagement. Encourage replies, DMs, and sign-ups that build a direct, high-value connection.
    

### **Focus on Fastest Path to Revenue**

*   **No-Brainer Offer:** Create a low-ticket, high-value product that’s an easy “yes” for your audience. This could be a mini-course, a toolkit, or a template that aligns with what you’re building.
    
*   **Waitlist for Main Course:** While you’re building in public, gather a waitlist for the main offering. Use the anticipation to nurture and pre-qualify leads.
    
*   **High-Leverage Channels:** Prioritize platforms where your audience is most likely to engage and convert. LinkedIn and Facebook for professional credibility, Instagram and TikTok for broader reach and discovery, and YouTube for in-depth, evergreen content.
    

### **Next Steps**

1.  **Finalize Your Anchor Content Format:** Decide whether it’s a newsletter, a LinkedIn article, or a YouTube video.
    
2.  **Draft the Re-engagement Email:** We’ll craft a compelling message to reintroduce yourself to your list, set expectations, and drive them toward your no-brainer offer or waitlist.
    
3.  **Create a Content Repurposing Workflow:** Set up a system to seamlessly turn your anchor content into micro-content pieces that drive continuous engagement.
    

Let’s start by zeroing in on the anchor content and the re-engagement email. Once you’re comfortable with those, we’ll move into repurposing strategies and scaling across the channels. Sound good?

### **Step-by-Step Strategy Outline (Neurodivergent-Friendly)**

*   **Focus:** Create one high-value anchor content piece.
    
*   **Format:** Choose between a LinkedIn article, a detailed Facebook post, or a newsletter to your email list.

*   **Focus:** Introduce a low-ticket, no-brainer offer that aligns with your new direction. This could be a mini-course, a toolkit, or a template.
    
*   **Format:** Promote this offer through your email list, LinkedIn, and Facebook with a sense of urgency or a limited-time angle.
    
*   **Action:** Use this offer to generate quick revenue and validate the market interest.

*   Create and publish your anchor content.

**Week 2: Micro-Content Repurposing**

**Week 3: Conversion & Monetization**

*   Promote it through all channels and the email list.
    
*   Start collecting feedback and use that to refine your next steps.
    

### **Why This Path?**

*   **Focused & Manageable:** You start with one piece of content and leverage it across multiple platforms, minimizing overwhelm.
    
*   **Quick Revenue:** The low-ticket offer generates cash flow without you having to produce a massive deliverable upfront.
    
*   **Validation:** You quickly test market interest and refine your approach based on real feedback.

## A:

> **“Give me a daily summary of only the labels that matter, sent somewhere I’ll actually check, with the ability to take action from there.”**

* * *

## **DAILY LABEL SUMMARY SYSTEM: What’s Possible Now**

### **Goal:**

*   Send a **daily summary of specific Gmail labels**
    
*   Deliver it to a place you’ll notice and interact with
    
*   Enable follow-up actions like reply, snooze, archive, tag, or forward
    

* * *

### ✅ **What You Can Do Right Now**

#### **Option A: Gmail + Google Apps Script + Slack/Chat (no Gemini required)**

Create a custom Google Apps Script that:

*   Checks Gmail daily at a set time
    
*   Pulls threads from specific labels (e.g. `1 - INBOUND`, `3 - PITCH IT`)
    
*   Formats a summary (subject, sender, snippet, link to reply)
    
*   Sends that summary via:
    
    *   Slack DM to yourself
        
    *   Google Chat (if integrated)
        
    *   Even SMS via Twilio if needed
        

And yes — we can include buttons like:

*   ✅ Archive
    
*   ✏️ Reply with canned response
    
*   ⏰ Snooze 24 hrs
    
*   ➕ Add to Notion/Tasks
    

> _This gives you visibility outside your inbox AND light interactivity_

#### **Option B: Notion Mail + Slack + Zapier or Make**

*   Notion Mail pulls the messages → dumps them into a Notion database
    
*   Zapier runs a daily digest of that database and sends a summary to Slack or Google Chat
    
*   You use buttons or slash commands to take light actions back in Notion (or flag for deeper review)
    

> _Best if you're already Notion-native and want everything piped into your OSOT_

#### **Option C: Gmail + Zapier + OpenAI + Slack/Chat**

*   Gmail label triggers summary generation
    
*   OpenAI condenses it (if you want real natural-language summaries)
    
*   Slack receives the digest — and buttons can trigger responses
    

* * *

### 🧪 Vibe Code "AFTER" Options (Emerging Tech Stack Ideas)

*   **Gemini 2.5 + Firebase + Workspace API**: This _will_ eventually allow intelligent summaries + proactive suggestions (like “Want me to reply to this intro email?”) — but right now, it’s dev-heavy and clunky
    
*   **Reclaim.ai + Zapier** combo: Could add time-blocked “reply windows” to your calendar + AI-powered summary Slack pings
    

* * *

### Mazinity Suggests:

Let’s start light + smart:

> **Build Option A: Gmail → Apps Script → Slack summary @10am daily**  
> Pulls from only the mission-critical labels.  
> Includes clear actions like: “Reply / Snooze / Archive / Forward / Tag”

Then later, we vibe-code deeper AI integrations once you're already flowing.

* * *

## **What You Should Build for Jerry in Notion**

Here’s your base system design — optimized for **built-in automations, relational databases**, and a clean UX for a team that’s part creative, part ops-driven.

* * *

### **1. Content Pipeline Database (Master Tracker)**

Each row = 1 video idea  
Core properties:

*   Script Title (linked to script database or Poppy import)
    
*   Status (Idea, Script Ready, Filming, Editing, Draft Ready, Scheduled, Posted)
    
*   Channel (multi-select: IG, YT Shorts, TikTok, etc.)
    
*   Priority
    
*   Assigned Roles (Owner: Jerry, Editor, SMM)
    
*   Due Date
    
*   Link to Drive Folder / Final Asset
    
*   Notes
    

**Built-In Notion Automations:**

*   When Status = “Draft Ready,” auto assign SMM + notify
    
*   When Status = “Scheduled,” auto move to “Posted” after due date passes
    

* * *

### **2. Script Source + Archive (Optional Database)**

Only if you want to capture historical script content and link it to videos.

Properties:

*   Script Name
    
*   Draft Version / Poppy Link
    
*   Status (Proofing, Approved)
    
*   Related Video Idea (relation to Content Pipeline)
    

* * *

### **3. Role-Specific Views**

Each team member sees what’s relevant to them:

*   **Jerry’s View:** Needs Review / Needs Approval
    
*   **Editor’s View:** Status = “Editing,” Assigned to Editor
    
*   **SMM’s View:** Status = “Draft Ready” or “Final Review”
    

* * *

### **4. Simple Publishing Calendar (Filtered View)**

*   Show only content where Status = Scheduled or Posted
    
*   Weekly view with card previews
    
*   Auto-move past dates to Posted
    

* * *

### **5. Caption + Asset Bank (Optional if SMM wants it)**

*   Upload final caption text + hashtags
    
*   Upload thumbnail/screenshot
    
*   Connect to final post URL (for portfolio or repurposing later)
    

* * *

## **Phase 2 Integration Ideas**

Later, if you want to expand:

*   **Make.com automation**: Pull Poppy board exports (JSON or Zapier-parsed) directly into the Content Pipeline
    
*   **AI Assist inside Notion**: Auto-suggest captions, hook edits, etc.
    
*   **Feedback loop**: Add “Debrief” property to record performance data
    

* * *

Jerry doesn’t need an AI system — he needs a **central command station** for his team.

## Q: 
Okay, either it’s way too late, or you’re over-estimating my ability to process all this right now (a lot of the first and a wee bit of the last)… Let me start with this. 1. I want Zapier or Make to automatically pull the final Poppy script outputs into Notion if at all possible without having to invest in the Poppy API upgrade. Is that possible? 2. Do you see an opportunity like I do to potentially use Poppy at the beginning of the is process not only to create the video script, but also to write the post copy also?

## A: 
Totally get it — you're running on fumes and asking the _exact right questions_ before the brain fog rolls in. So let’s simplify this down to pure signal:

* * *

### **1. Can we auto-pull Poppy scripts into Notion via Zapier or Make _without_ upgrading to Poppy’s API plan?**

**Short answer: Not right now.**  
Poppy **doesn’t yet have a public Zapier/Make integration** or open webhook triggers unless you’re on their higher-tier API plan. You’d need one of these workarounds:

#### **Low-effort workaround (recommended for now):**

*   **Use Poppy’s export/download/share feature**
    
*   Drop the scripts into a dedicated Gmail label or Google Drive folder
    
*   Use **Zapier/Make to watch that label/folder** and auto-create a Notion database entry when a new file hits
    

> _Result:_ Final scripts go from Drive → Notion content pipeline without upgrading your plan or manually copying.

Let me know if you want me to build or map that scenario. It’s efficient, budget-friendly, and dopamine-proof.

* * *

### **2. Can Poppy be used to write both video scripts _and_ post captions?**

**YES. Huge opportunity here.**  
If you steer the Poppy prompt intentionally, it can generate:

*   A short-form video script for IG/TikTok/Shorts
    
*   Caption text with call-to-action, hashtags, or emotion-based hooks
    
*   Even title options or thumbnail hook ideas
    

So yeah — build the Notion framework _assuming that Poppy is doing the heavy-lift content generation at the front_, and your system is catching and routing it where needed (scripts → editing, captions → publishing).

* * *

### TL;DR for sleepy Patty:

*   **Auto-import** from Poppy to Notion = possible via Drive/Gmail workaround
    
*   **Dual-purpose Poppy prompt** = YES, use it for both script + post copy (just tweak your prompt style a bit)
    

When you’re ready to systematize this into something your brain _wants_ to use, I’ll have a 5-field Notion table and one Make scenario waiting with your name on it.

## **Step-by-Step: Poppy → Notion (Without API Upgrade)**

_Budget-friendly, automation-ready workaround_

### **How It Works:**

1.  **User exports final scripts from Poppy**
    
    *   Poppy allows **copy**, **download**, or **share/export** of output
        
    *   Export each final script as either a text file or a Google Doc (whichever is easiest)
        
2.  **Drop into Google Drive**
    
    *   Set up a folder like: `Poppy Script Drops`
        
    *   He (or his assistant) moves finalized scripts into that folder manually or via share
        
3.  **Use Make or Zapier to watch that Drive folder**
    
    *   Trigger: New file added
        
    *   Action: Create new item in **Notion Content Pipeline**
        
        *   Title = file name
            
        *   Script = file contents (or a link to the file if using Google Docs)
            
        *   Status = “Script Ready”
            
        *   Assigned To = Jerry
            
        *   Due Date = optional
            
4.  **Notion picks up from there**
    
    *   Team jumps in using filtered views
        
    *   Editor, SMM, etc. see what’s ready for them in sequence
        

> **Bonus:** Add a checkbox called “Auto-Debrief?” in Notion so once posted, the SMM can flag if the piece needs follow-up analysis.

* * *

Plenty for this unless he’s pushing out hundreds of scripts a week (lol he’s not).

> “If and when you scale up volume, Make grows with you — but we’ll start with the free tier so you’re not paying for tech you’re not using.”

*   A **hell yes** for someone who values their time
    
*   **Underpriced**, honestly, if this saves his team even 5 hours/week
    
*   NOT pricing you out — you’re solving a real pain point with a clear ROI

## A: 
Yessss, let’s crack this wide open while he’s still warm and curious.

He’s asking about **Option 2** — which, in this case, means:

> “Can this thing publish to Instagram once approved in Notion?”

Short answer: **Yes, but it’s a custom build that requires API wizardry, third-party connection tools (like Metricool, Publer, Later, Buffer, or Facebook Graph API), and scoped automation logic.**

* * *

## 🔧 OPTION 2: “Publish to IG from Notion” Automation Build (via Make)

### **What It Actually Entails:**

#### **1. Approved → Trigger Event**

*   Status in Notion changes to “Approved for IG”
    
*   OR checkbox marked “Publish to IG”
    
*   That becomes the trigger for Make
    

#### **2. Grab Content From Notion**

*   Pull caption (text)
    
*   Pull video asset link (hosted in Drive or Dropbox, or a direct upload path)
    
*   Pull platform tag = Instagram
    

#### **3. Pass to Social Publishing Tool**

Unless you want to get deep with the Facebook/IG Graph API (read: painful), you’ll pass this content to:

✅ **Metricool (best all-around)  
✅ Buffer (simple but clean)  
✅ Publer (affordable and functional)**

Make can integrate with these to:

*   Upload media
    
*   Add caption
    
*   Schedule immediately or at pre-defined time
    
*   Confirm post action back into Notion (optional)
    

#### **4. Error Handling & Logs**

*   If the asset doesn’t load or the platform returns an error, you’ll want to log it or flag it in Notion so someone can resolve it
    

* * *

## 🧾 Pricing for Option 2

This is **not a light add-on** — it’s a standalone mini-project, because it involves:

*   More Make steps (more operations = possible paid tier)
    
*   Testing across platforms
    
*   Platform auth setup
    
*   Error handling
    
*   Possibly helping him register for and connect a tool like Metricool
    

### **Recommended Price Range:**

*   **$450–$600 USD** one-time  
    (Assumes IG only — single-channel logic, no advanced scheduling UI)
    
*   **+$150–250** if he wants this expanded to TikTok or YouTube Shorts later
    

### **Deliverables:**

*   Automation from “Approved in Notion” → IG post via Metricool/Buffer
    
*   Setup + config of chosen publishing platform
    
*   SOP or Loom for using the system
    
*   Error handling: soft fail notification if asset isn’t found or auth fails
    

* * *

Want me to draft the optional add-on scope and pricing language so it’s ready to paste into the proposal when he says “Cool, show me that too”?

## Q: 
Two questions to clarify: FIRST: Pull from Notion, Step 1 you said: Video URL (must be publicly accessible, not Drive or Dropbox) If I set the sharing permissions for the folder in G Drive these are in to anyone with the link can view/comment/edit, we could use GDrive still for the finished Reels, correct? SECOND: Doesn't it make complete sense to build this ONTO the Make automation we're using to move the Poppy copy into Notion?

## A: 
💯 Let’s clarify both like the pro you are:

* * *

### **FIRST: Can we use Google Drive for the Reels if permissions are set to 'Anyone with the link'?**

**Unfortunately… no.**  
Even if the Drive file is shared publicly, **Instagram’s API cannot fetch media from Google Drive or Dropbox**. They require a **direct file URL** — like from a CDN (Content Delivery Network) or a raw file host.

Why? Because Google Drive uses masked URLs that don’t serve raw content headers — and IG needs a clean `.mp4` or image file endpoint.

#### ✅ Instead:

Use a **public media host** like:

*   [**Bunny.net**](https://bunny.net) (super cheap + fast CDN, ND-friendly)
    
*   AWS S3 (if someone already has it setup)
    
*   Cloudinary (free tier, great for small media)
    
*   Even Imgur for images only (quick and dirty)
    

If needed, I can help you:

*   Set up a basic Bunny.net bucket
    
*   Connect Make to upload the file there first
    
*   Then pass that public URL to Instagram
    

_It’s one extra step — but it makes this all work reliably._

* * *

### **SECOND: Can this IG automation be layered onto the Poppy→Notion Make scenario?**

**YES — and it’s smart AF to do it that way.**

Here’s how we stack it:

1.  **Scenario Part 1:**
    
    *   Poppy final script gets dropped in Drive
        
    *   Make pulls the content + creates a new Notion entry
        
    *   Caption and video idea land in “Script Ready” status
        
2.  **Scenario Part 2:**
    
    *   You manually (or auto via rule) change Notion status to “Approved for IG”
        
    *   Make watches for that status change
        
    *   It grabs the caption + IG-ready video URL
        
    *   Posts to Instagram via Instagram for Business
        
    *   Updates Notion entry with “Published” status
        

You’re just **chaining two flows in one scenario** — _clean_, modular, and no extra overhead.

* * *

So yes:

*   ✅ _Build it into the same Make scenario_
    
*   ❌ _Don’t rely on Google Drive for final media links_ — use a proper CDN for IG to play nice
    

Want me to now write up the **revised add-on proposal section** for Jerry, scoped exactly as “IG automation on top of your existing flow”? You’re two steps from yes.

## Q: 
Wait, again, if I watch this video, what I see is the dude is pulling the video URL from Airtable, so that's his repository for the Reel. Couldn't we do the same with Notion? Use it for storage of the video? Or no?

## A: 
Ahhh, this is _such_ a great catch — and your instincts are spot-on. Let’s get really clear here:

* * *

### 🧠 The Airtable “Video URL” Trick in the Video

In the demo you watched, the creator is using **Airtable as the place to store the video link**, _but not the host itself._

He’s either:

1.  Uploading the video somewhere public (like Imgur, Bunny, S3, or similar)
    
2.  Storing the **publicly accessible URL** in Airtable
    
3.  Using Airtable only as a **pointer** — not as the media host
    

🚫 Airtable itself isn’t serving the file in a way Instagram’s API accepts. It just holds a string — the video’s link — that’s already hosted elsewhere.

* * *

### ❌ Why Notion Can’t Be the Video Host Either

Even if you upload the video into Notion or embed it in a database:

*   The **video file** is not publicly served as a raw media URL
    
*   Instagram’s API needs a **direct, no-login, no-wrapper** file endpoint (like `https://cdn.host/video.mp4`)
    
*   Notion's file links require cookies/auth headers and timeout after a short period
    

Same goes for:

*   Google Drive
    
*   Dropbox
    
*   OneDrive
    

They don’t serve media in a **"fetchable-by-robot"** format that Instagram needs.

* * *

### ✅ So What _Does_ Work?

Here’s what IG’s API _will_ accept for video/photo links:

*   **Bunny.net**
    
*   **Cloudinary** (great free plan, supports video uploads)
    
*   **AWS S3** (requires setup, but works well)
    
*   **Imgur** (for photos only)
    

Make.com can upload the file to one of those _during your scenario_ and return a link — super slick.

* * *

### TL;DR

| Tool | Can Store the File | Can Serve It to IG? |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Notion | ✅ (kind of) | ❌ |
| Airtable | ✅ | ❌ (just stores URLs) |
| Google Drive | ✅ | ❌ |
| Bunny/CDN | ✅ | ✅ |
| Cloudinary | ✅ | ✅ |

So sadly, **you can’t host your IG-ready Reels directly from Notion or Drive** — but you can point to a CDN URL _from_ Notion and let Make handle the rest.

Want help picking the best CDN for this based on his team/tools? Or want me to bake this into the final IG automation proposal copy now?

#### Why it’s a great fit:

*   ✅ Native Make integration
    
*   ✅ Can upload videos via URL or directly from Make
    
*   ✅ Can serve video in IG-compatible formats (direct file URLs)

    *   **10 GB storage / 20 GB bandwidth**
        
    *   More than enough for short Reels if you delete after post
        

#### Also:

*   ✅ Easy file deletion via API after publish
    
*   ✅ Great UI for reviewing files manually if needed
    
*   ❌ No watermarking or delays like some “free file hosts”
    

* * *

## 🔧 Step 2: Flow Summary for IG Auto-Publish

**MAKE Scenario:**

1.  **Trigger:** Notion entry status = “Approved for IG”
    
2.  **Step:** Pull video file from Notion/Drive (must be direct link)
    
3.  **Step:** Upload video to Cloudinary (Make module)
    
4.  **Step:** Send post to IG via Instagram for Business module
    
5.  **Step:** If post succeeds, use Cloudinary module to **delete the file**
    
6.  **Step:** Update Notion entry → “Published” + add timestamp or IG link
    

> This gives you **zero bloat**, one-touch publishing, and rotating file storage.

* * *

## Q: 
Wait, if we use Cloudinary's free tier, there's watermarks? Nope, not likely gonna be an option. What's our other choice?

## A: 
⚠️ **Totally fair — and smart to double-check.**

Here’s the truth:  
**Cloudinary’s free tier does _not_ watermark videos by default.**  
But—some users have reported watermarking **only if** you exceed the free tier or trigger heavy “transformations” (like resizing, compression, etc.).

Since we're:

*   Uploading **short Reels** (small file sizes)
    
*   Not doing any advanced transformations
    
*   Deleting files post-publish
    

👉 **You're safe** within the 10GB storage + 20GB bandwidth **without watermarking** — _as long as you clean up regularly._

* * *

### BUT... if you'd rather avoid _any_ risk of branding/watermark issues?

Let’s go **Bunny.net** — the _cleanest, most generous, no-frills option_ for indie creators.

* * *

## 🐇 **Bunny.net: The Best Alternative**

### ✅ Why it’s awesome:

*   **$1/month minimum** (not free, but ultra-cheap — think $12/year to sleep easy)
    
*   CDN-grade hosting built for media (serves .mp4s fast and clean)
    
*   No watermarking. No file transformations.
    
*   Can upload via API or FTP
    
*   Works perfectly with Make via HTTP module (easy setup)
    

### Bunny’s Pricing:

*   **$0.01/GB storage**
    
*   **$0.01/GB bandwidth**
    
*   First **$1/month** minimum charge applies (so it’s predictable)
    

> 1GB storage = ~30–50 Reels  
> Deleting after posting = you’ll probably never hit 1GB/month

* * *

### Final Rec:

If Jerry can spare **$1/month**, Bunny.net is **100% the pro move** —  
✅ Clean delivery  
✅ Zero branding risk  
✅ Reliable AF

## Q: 
“Okay, can you tell me now if you processed all that?”

## A: 
Absolutely! Here’s the gist of what you’re doing:

1.  **Booking and Labeling:**
    
    *   When someone books a call through Calendly, it syncs to your Google Calendar and sends a notification email to Gmail.
        
    *   These emails get automatically labeled based on the day of the week the call is scheduled for.
        
2.  **Nightly Automation:**
    
    *   Each evening, a process runs that looks at the emails labeled for the next day’s calls.
        
    *   It extracts the relevant details (name, date, time in your time zone, phone number, email, time zone) and puts them into a Google Sheet.
        
3.  **Task Creation:**
    
    *   The information from the Google Sheet is then used to create a set of subtasks (or possibly events) in your Google Calendar for the following day, so you have a clear picture of who you need to text and when.
        
    *   This makes it easier for you to preschedule or manually send those reminder texts at the right time, ensuring the high show-up rate.
        
4.  **Time Zone Conversion:**
    
    *   Since your clients are from all over the world and their time zones can vary (and aren’t always in the same format), the automation also normalizes these time zones into a standard format that you can easily reference. This way, you know exactly when to send those reminders without having to do mental math every single time.
        

So essentially, this two-step process pulls in all the booking info from Gmail, organizes it in a Google Sheet, converts the time zones, and then sets up your daily tasks so you can seamlessly send out those reminders.

That all makes perfect sense, and it’s a really efficient way to handle it! Let’s talk about any specific tweaks or challenges you need help with next.

## Q:

## A:

1.  \*\*Pres

## Q: 
“I'm sorry, Ms. Inouye, please continue.”

## A: 
No problem! Let’s recap the key points:

1.  **Prescheduled Texts for iPhone Users:**
    
    *   If the person has an iPhone, you can pre-schedule their reminder texts the night before. If not, any incomplete tasks from the previous night’s automation get pushed to the following morning. This way, you have a reminder on your calendar to manually send those texts to non-iPhone users. The subtasks in your calendar include the person’s first name, the time of the call in their time zone (with the abbreviation), the day and date of the call, and their phone number.
        
2.  **Slack Reminders:**
    
    *   In the evening, after the automation runs and updates the Google Sheet and your Google Calendar, a Slack reminder is sent via a webhook to prompt you to schedule those texts for the next day’s calls. In the morning, another Slack reminder ensures you don’t forget to send out any manual texts.
        
3.  **Handling Transferred Calls:**
    
    *   Sometimes other agents transfer calls to you, and this can happen on short notice. When you accept ownership of the event in Google Calendar, the code updates the event title to indicate it’s with you (e.g., "[with Patty]").
        
4.  **Including Transferred Calls in the Automation:**
    
    *   To ensure these transferred calls are also part of the reminder system, the code checks your calendar for upcoming events with a specific keyword (like "Onboarding"). If it finds a matching event that wasn’t originally in the Gmail data, it pulls that information directly from the calendar and adds it to the Google Sheet. This ensures that any last-minute or rescheduled calls are included in the reminder sequence.
        

In short, your automation not only handles regular bookings but also adapts to last-minute transfers and reschedules. It keeps everything organized so you never miss a beat and can continue providing that personal touch with your reminders.

That’s a solid and comprehensive system you’ve got!

Aborting.`); return; } // Get today's date and time range for calendar search const today = new Date(); const todayStart = new Date(today); todayStart.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0); // Start of today const todayEnd = new Date(todayStart); let processedCount = 0; let skippedCount = 0; if (calendarEvents && calendarEvents.length > 0) { Logger.log(`Found ${calendarEvents.length} events on Calendar for today.`); for (const event of calendarEvents) { // Check if the current user is the organizer AND the tag is NOT already in the title // Note: Checking organizer might not be perfect if transfer logic is complex. // A more robust check might involve looking for attendees or specific event properties. const currentUserEmail = Session.getActiveUser().getEmail(); const isOrganizer = event.organizer && event.organizer.email === currentUserEmail; const hasUpdateTag = event.summary && event.summary.includes(updateTag); const isNotCancelled = event.status !== 'cancelled'; if (isOrganizer && !hasUpdateTag && isNotCancelled) { Logger.log(`Found potential transferred event: "${event.summary}" (ID: ${event.id}) at ${event.start.dateTime || event.start.date}`); // --- Extract Contact Details from the Event Description --- let contactName = 'Unknown Contact'; let contactEmail = null; let contactPhone = 'N/A'; let attendeeTzAbbrev = 'Unknown TZ'; let attendeeTzFull = 'Unknown Time Zone'; let yourTimestampFromDescription = null; // To capture the "Event Date/Time" string if present const description = event.description; if (description) { Logger.log("Attempting to extract details from Calendar event description..."); const descLines = description.split('\\n'); let foundDescName = false; let foundDescEmail = false; let foundDescPhone = false; let foundDescTZ = false; let foundDescTimestamp = false; for (const line of descLines) { const trimmedLine = line.trim(); if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee:') && !foundDescName) { contactName = trimmedLine.substring('Invitee:'.length).trim(); foundDescName = true; } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee Email:') && !foundDescEmail) { contactEmail = trimmedLine.substring('Invitee Email:'.length).trim(); if (contactEmail && !contactEmail.includes('@')) contactEmail = null; // Basic validation if (contactEmail) foundDescEmail = true; } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Text Reminder Number:') && !foundDescPhone) { contactPhone = trimmedLine.substring('Text Reminder Number:'.length).trim(); foundDescPhone = true; } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Phone Number:') && !foundDescPhone) { contactPhone = trimmedLine.substring('Phone Number:'.length).trim(); foundDescPhone = true; } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee Time Zone:') && !foundDescTZ) { const tzMatch = trimmedLine.match(/Invitee Time Zone:\\s\*(.\*?)\\s\*\\(([^)]+)\\)$/); if (tzMatch && tzMatch[1] && tzMatch[2]) { attendeeTzFull = tzMatch[1].trim(); attendeeTzAbbrev = tzMatch[2].trim(); foundDescTZ = true; } else { // Fallback if format is different if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee Time Zone:')) { attendeeTzFull = trimmedLine.substring('Invitee Time Zone:'.length).trim(); foundDescTZ = true; } } } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Event Date/Time:') && !foundDescTimestamp) { yourTimestampFromDescription = trimmedLine.substring('Event Date/Time:'.length).trim(); foundDescTimestamp = true; } // Stop if we found all key info from description if (foundDescName && foundDescEmail && foundDescPhone && foundDescTZ && foundDescTimestamp) { break; } } Logger.log(`Extracted from description - Name: ${contactName}, Email: ${contactEmail}, Phone: ${contactPhone}, TZ Abbrev: ${attendeeTzAbbrev}, TZ Full: ${attendeeTzFull}, Timestamp: ${yourTimestampFromDescription}`); } else { Logger.log("No description found for this transferred event."); } // Use the event start time as the timestamp if not found in description const yourTimestamp = yourTimestampFromDescription || (event.start.dateTime ? Utilities.formatDate(new Date(event.start.dateTime), TIMEZONE, "MMM dd,yyyy h:mm a") : (event.start.date ? Utilities.formatDate(new Date(event.start.date), TIMEZONE, "MMM dd,yyyy") : 'Unknown Time')); if (!contactEmail) { Logger.log(`Skipping processing transferred event "${event.summary}" (ID: ${event.id}) - Could not extract a valid contact email from description or attendees.`); skippedCount++; // Optionally log to sheet with a skipped status here if needed continue; // Skip to the next event } // --- Update Event Title in Calendar --- const newTitle = `${event.summary} ${updateTag}`; try { const updatedEvent = Calendar.Events.patch({ summary: newTitle }, 'primary', event.id); Logger.log(`Successfully updated event title to: "${updatedEvent.summary}"`); // --- Log Details to Sheet --- // Create a details object matching the expected sheet format const detailsToLog = { email: contactEmail, name: contactName, phone: contactPhone, attendeeTzAbbrev: attendeeTzAbbrev, attendeeTzFull: attendeeTzFull, yourTimestamp: yourTimestamp // Use the timestamp determined above }; // Log to sheet with a specific status indicating it was from a transferred event logToSheet(detailsToLog, todayStart, `Transferred Event: ${event.summary}`, `CALENDAR_${event.id}`, 'Transferred - Processed'); processedCount++; } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error updating event title or logging to sheet for event "${event.summary}" (ID: ${event.id}): ${e}`); skippedCount++; // Optionally log to sheet with an error status here if needed } } else { // Event is not owned by the user, already has the tag, or is cancelled Logger.log(`Skipping event "${event.summary}" (ID: ${event.id}) - Not owned by user, already tagged, or cancelled.`); skippedCount++; } } } else { Logger.log("No events found on Calendar for today."); } Logger.log(`Finished processTransferredEvents. Processed ${processedCount} transferred events, Skipped ${skippedCount} events.`); } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error searching Calendar for transferred events: ${e}`); } } /\*\* \* Extracts appointment details from a Gmail message body based on provided sample format. \* Extracts Name, Phone, Invitee Time Zone Abbrev, Invitee Time Zone Full, Event Date/Time (full string), and Email. \* @param {GmailMessage} message The Gmail message object. \* @returns {object | null} An object containing extracted details or null if extraction fails. \*/ function extractAppointmentDetails(message) { const body = message.getPlainTextBody(); const lines = body.split('\\n'); let name = null; let phone = null; let attendeeTzAbbrev = null; let attendeeTzFull = null; let yourTimestamp = null; // This will capture the "Event Date/Time" string let email = null; // Use flags to know when to stop searching for a specific piece of info let foundName = false; let foundPhone = false; let foundAttendeeTz = false; // Covers both abbrev and full let foundYourTimestamp = false; let foundEmail = false; for (const line of lines) { const trimmedLine = line.trim(); // Look for "Invitee:" for Name if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee:')) { name = trimmedLine.substring('Invitee:'.length).trim(); foundName = true; // Look for "Text Reminder Number:" or "Phone Number:" for Phone } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Text Reminder Number:') && !foundPhone) { phone = trimmedLine.substring('Text Reminder Number:'.length).trim(); foundPhone = true; } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Phone Number:') && !foundPhone) { // Also check for "Phone Number:" phone = trimmedLine.substring('Phone Number:'.length).trim(); foundPhone = true; // Look for "Invitee Time Zone:" for Time Zone Full and Abbrev } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee Time Zone:') && !foundAttendeeTz) { const tzMatch = trimmedLine.match(/Invitee Time Zone:\\s\*(.\*?)\\s\*\\(([^)]+)\\)$/); if (tzMatch && tzMatch[1] && tzMatch[2]) { attendeeTzFull = tzMatch[1].trim(); attendeeTzAbbrev = tzMatch[2].trim(); foundAttendeeTz = true; } else { // Fallback if the format doesn't have the (Abbrev) part if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee Time Zone:')) { attendeeTzFull = trimmedLine.substring('Invitee Time Zone:'.length).trim(); // Cannot get abbreviation in this case, abbrev remains null foundAttendeeTz = true; // Found something for TZ } } // Look for "Event Date/Time:" for the timestamp string } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Event Date/Time:') && !foundYourTimestamp) { yourTimestamp = trimmedLine.substring('Event Date/Time:'.length).trim(); foundYourTimestamp = true; // Look for "Invitee Email:" for Email } else if (trimmedLine.startsWith('Invitee Email:') && !foundEmail) { email = trimmedLine.substring('Invitee Email:'.length).trim(); // Basic validation for email format if (email && !email.includes('@')) { // Check email is not empty before validating Logger.log(`Warning: Extracted potential email "${email}" doesn't contain '@'.`); email = null; // Treat as not found if it doesn't look like an email } if (email) foundEmail = true; // Only set flag if email was successfully extracted/validated } // Stop processing lines if we've found all the required information if (foundName && foundPhone && foundAttendeeTz && foundYourTimestamp && foundEmail) { break; } } // Basic validation: ensure required fields were found // Require Name, Phone, TZ Abbrev (or Full), Your Timestamp, and Email if (name && phone && (attendeeTzAbbrev || attendeeTzFull) && yourTimestamp && email) { Logger.log(`Extracted - Name: ${name}, Phone: ${phone}, TZ Abbrev: ${attendeeTzAbbrev}, TZ Full: ${attendeeTzFull}, Your Timestamp: ${yourTimestamp}, Email: ${email}`); return { name, phone, attendeeTzAbbrev, attendeeTzFull, yourTimestamp, email }; } else { Logger.log(`Failed to extract *all* required details from message: ${message.getSubject()} (ID: ${message.getId()})`); Logger.log(`Partial: Name=${name}, Phone=${phone}, TZ Abbrev=${attendeeTzAbbrev}, TZ Full=${attendeeTzFull}, YourTimestamp=${yourTimestamp}, Email=${email}`); // Return null if any required field is missing return null; } } /\*\* \* Main function to process emails and create the evening batch task. \* Includes a check against Google Calendar to ensure the event is still valid. \* Formats the evening task title for easy manual texting, including time in ATTENDEE TZ. \* Should be triggered daily in the evening (around 18:00). \*/ function processAppointmentsAndCreateEveningTask() { Logger.log('Starting processAppointmentsAndCreateEveningTask (Format Evening Task for Attendee TZ)...'); // Updated log message const ss = SpreadsheetApp.openById(SPREADSHEET_ID); const sheet = ss.getSheetByName(SHEET_NAME); if (!sheet) { Logger.log(`Error: Sheet not found with name ${SHEET_NAME}. Aborting.`); return; } // Determine the target appointment date (tomorrow or next Monday) const today = new Date(); let dayOfWeek = today.getDay(); // 0 for Sunday, 1 for Monday, ..., 5 for Friday, 6 for Saturday // --- TEMPORARY FOR TESTING FRIDAY-TO-MONDAY LOGIC --- // Uncomment the line below to make the script think today is Friday (day 5) // dayOfWeek = 5; // --- END TEMPORARY TEST CODE --- let daysToAdd = 1; // Default to tomorrow let targetDate = new Date(today); if (dayOfWeek === 5) { // If today is Friday daysToAdd = 3; // Add 3 days to get to Monday targetDate.setDate(targetDate.getDate() + daysToAdd); } else if (dayOfWeek === 6) { // If today is Saturday (and no Saturday label) Logger.log("Today is Saturday. No Gmail label configured for Saturday. Skipping."); return; // Exit the script } else if (dayOfWeek === 0) { // If today is Sunday (and no Sunday label) Logger.log("Today is Sunday. No Gmail label configured for Sunday. Skipping."); return; // Exit the script } else { // Any other day (Mon-Thurs), process for tomorrow targetDate.setDate(targetDate.getDate() + daysToAdd); // Use targetDate here to add days correctly } // Reset time components of target date for reliable comparison and task setting targetDate.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0); const targetDayName = getDayName(targetDate); const searchLabel = getGmailLabelForDay(targetDayName); if (!searchLabel) { // This check is mostly for safety, the logic above should handle Mon-Fri correctly Logger.log(`No Gmail label defined in the script configuration for ${targetDayName}. Skipping.`); return; // Exit the script if no label is configured } Logger.log(`Calculated Target Appointment Date: ${Utilities.formatDate(targetDate, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd")}. Looking for UNREAD emails with label: "${searchLabel}" from any date.`); // --- MODIFIED GMAIL SEARCH QUERY (Removed is:unread) --- // Look for any email with the target label (will check unread status later) const searchQuery = `label:"${searchLabel}"`; Logger.log(`Searching Gmail with query: "${searchQuery}"`); let processedCount = 0; const appointmentsToProcess = []; // Array to hold details for task creation try { const threads = GmailApp.search(searchQuery); threads.forEach(thread => { const messages = thread.getMessages(); messages.forEach(message => { // --- NEW: Check unread status here --- if (!message.isUnread()) { Logger.log(`Skipping read message: ${message.getSubject()}`); return; // Skip if the message is already read } const details = extractAppointmentDetails(message); // Ensure core details needed for check/log are present: email, timestamp, and at least one TZ field if (details && details.email && details.yourTimestamp && (details.attendeeTzAbbrev || details.attendeeTzFull)) { // --- Validate the extracted appointment date --- try { // Attempt to parse the date part from the extracted timestamp string // Based on sample: "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" // We need to extract "Thursday, April 24, 2025" const datePartMatch = details.yourTimestamp.match(/-\\s\*(.\*?)\\s\*\\(/); // Capture text between "-" and "(" let extractedDatePart = ''; if (datePartMatch && datePartMatch[1]) { extractedDatePart = datePartMatch[1].trim(); } else { throw new Error("Could not find date part in timestamp string."); } const extractedAppointmentDate = new Date(extractedDatePart); extractedAppointmentDate.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0); // Reset time for comparison // Compare the extracted date to the calculated target date if (extractedAppointmentDate.getTime() === targetDate.getTime()) { Logger.log(`Extracted appointment date (${Utilities.formatDate(extractedAppointmentDate, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd")}) matches target date. Proceeding to Calendar check for email: ${message.getSubject()}`); // --- Calendar Check --- const contactEmail = details.email; const contactName = details.name; // Use name for logging/identification const appointmentDateString = Utilities.formatDate(targetDate, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd"); // Use the validated targetDate string try { // Get the start and end of the appointment day for calendar search let appointmentDate = new Date(appointmentDateString); // Use the validated targetDate // Set time to start of day for search range appointmentDate.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0); const searchStartTime = appointmentDate.toISOString(); let appointmentEndDate = new Date(appointmentDate); appointmentEndDate.setDate(appointmentEndDate.getDate() + 1); // Search until the start of the next day const searchEndTime = appointmentEndDate.toISOString(); Logger.log(`Searching Calendar for events for ${contactName} (${contactEmail}) between ${searchStartTime} and ${searchEndTime}`); // Search for events involving this email within the appointment day const calendarEvents = Calendar.Events.list('primary', { timeMin: searchStartTime, timeMax: searchEndTime, q: contactEmail, // Search query for the email address singleEvents: true, // Expand recurring events orderBy: 'startTime', }).items; let foundValidEvent = null; if (calendarEvents && calendarEvents.length > 0) { Logger.log(`Found ${calendarEvents.length} potential events for ${contactName}.`); // Iterate through found events to find a match and check status for (const event of calendarEvents) { // Basic check: Is the event not cancelled and does it involve this attendee? // More robust checks could compare start time or title if needed. const isAttendeePresent = event.attendees && event.attendees.some(attendee => attendee.email === contactEmail && !attendee.self); // Check if attendee is present and not self const isNotCancelled = event.status !== 'cancelled'; if (isNotCancelled && isAttendeePresent) { Logger.log(`Found valid event for ${contactName}: "${event.summary}" (ID: ${event.id}) at ${event.start.dateTime || event.start.date}`); foundValidEvent = event; break; // Found a valid event, no need to check others } else { Logger.log(`Skipping event for ${contactName} "${event.summary}" (ID: ${event.id}) - Status: ${event.status}, Attendee Present: ${isAttendeePresent}`); } } } else { Logger.log(`No events found for ${contactName} (${contactEmail}) on ${appointmentDateString}.`); } // --- End Calendar Check --- if (foundValidEvent) { Logger.log(`Calendar event found and valid for ${contactName}. Logging to sheet and adding to process list.`); // Log to sheet with 'Processed' status logToSheet(details, targetDate, message.getSubject(), message.getId(), 'Processed'); appointmentsToProcess.push({ details, emailId: message.getId() }); // Add to array for task creation processedCount++; // Mark the email as read after processing message.markRead(); Logger.log(`Marked email as read: ${message.getSubject()}`); } else { // Event not found or not valid in Calendar Logger.log(`Calendar event not found or invalid for ${contactName} (${contactEmail}) on ${appointmentDateString}. Skipping task creation.`); // Log to sheet with skipped status logToSheet(details, targetDate, message.getSubject(), message.getId(), 'Skipped - Event Not Found/Invalid'); // Do NOT mark as read, leave for manual review } } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error during Calendar check for ${contactName} (${contactEmail}): ${e}`); // Log to sheet with error status logToSheet(details, targetDate, message.getSubject(), message.getId(), 'Skipped - Calendar Check Error'); // Do NOT mark as read, leave for manual review } } else { Logger.log(`Extracted appointment date (${Utilities.formatDate(extractedAppointmentDate, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd")}) does NOT match target date (${Utilities.formatDate(targetDate, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd")}). Skipping email: ${message.getSubject()}`); // Log to sheet with skipped status logToSheet(details, targetDate, message.getSubject(), message.getId(), 'Skipped - Date Mismatch'); // Do NOT mark as read, leave for manual review if needed } } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error parsing date from extracted timestamp "${details.yourTimestamp}" for email ${message.getSubject()}: ${e}`); Logger.log("Skipping email due to date parsing error."); // Log to sheet with skipped status logToSheet(details, targetDate, message.getSubject(), message.getId(), 'Skipped - Date Parse Error'); // Do NOT mark as read, leave for manual review } } else { // If extraction of core details failed, skip processing and leave unread Logger.log(`Skipping email due to extraction failure: ${message.getSubject()}`); // Note: We don't log to sheet here because core details weren't extracted. // Do NOT mark as read, leave for manual review } }); }); } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error searching Gmail or processing messages: ${e}`); // Continue to task creation even if email processing had errors, // in case some items were logged before the error. } Logger.log(`Found and processed ${processedCount} new appointment emails for ${targetDayName} matching the target date and calendar check.`); // --- Create the Evening Batch Task --- if (appointmentsToProcess.length > 0) { Logger.log('Creating evening batch task...'); const eveningTaskList = getOrCreateTaskList(EVENING_TASK_LIST_NAME); // Create the parent task for the day's batch // Task due date should be the day of the appointment (targetDate) const batchTaskTitle = `Send Reminders for ${Utilities.formatDate(targetDate, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd")} Appointments`; // Set the due date and time for the parent task const eveningTaskDueDate = new Date(targetDate); // Start with the appointment date const eveningTimeParts = EVENING_TASK_TIME.split(':'); eveningTaskDueDate.setHours(parseInt(eveningTimeParts[0], 10), parseInt(eveningTimeParts[1], 10), 0, 0); const eveningTaskDueDateISO = eveningTaskDueDate.toISOString(); const parentTask = Tasks.Tasks.insert({ title: batchTaskTitle, due: eveningTaskDueDateISO, notes: "Automated reminder batch. Send texts to attendees below." }, eveningTaskList.id); Logger.log(`Created parent task: "${parentTask.title}" (ID: ${parentTask.id})" due ${eveningTaskDueDateISO}`); // Get data range in sheet to find the rows we just added with 'Processed' status const data = sheet.getDataRange().getValues(); const header = data.shift(); // Remove header row // Find column indices dynamically based on header row const emailIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Email ID'); // Use Email ID to find the row reliably const statusColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Status'); const eveningTaskIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Evening Task ID'); const eveningParentTaskIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Evening Parent Task ID'); // Indices needed to build the task title (using original extraction names for clarity here) const nameColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Name'); const yourTimestampColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Meeting Timestamp (Your TZ)'); // e.g., "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" const tzAbbrevColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Time Zone Abbrev'); // e.g., "CET" const tzFullColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Time Zone Full'); // Use full for conversion const phoneColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Cell Phone'); // e.g., "+1-555-1212" const appointmentDateColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Appointment Date (Your TZ)'); // Needed for sheet lookup if (emailIdColumnIndex === -1 || statusColumnIndex === -1 || eveningTaskIdColumnIndex === -1 || eveningParentTaskIdColumnIndex === -1 || nameColumnIndex === -1 || yourTimestampColumnIndex === -1 || tzAbbrevColumnIndex === -1 || tzFullColumnIndex === -1 || phoneColumnIndex === -1 || appointmentDateColumnIndex === -1) { Logger.log("Error: Missing required columns in sheet header row. Cannot create tasks or update sheet status."); Logger.log("Required headers: 'Email ID', 'Meeting Timestamp (Your TZ)', 'Appointment Date (Your TZ)', 'Contact Name', 'Contact Cell Phone', 'Contact Time Zone Abbrev', 'Contact Time Zone Full', 'Status', 'Evening Task ID', 'Evening Parent Task ID', 'Morning Task ID', 'Morning Parent Task ID'"); return; } // Filter data rows to find the ones just added with 'Processed' status by this run const processedAppointmentRows = data.filter(row => row[statusColumnIndex] === 'Processed' && appointmentsToProcess.some(ap => ap.emailId === row[emailIdColumnIndex]) // Ensure email ID is one we just processed and passed checks ); // Iterate through the filtered rows and create subtasks processedAppointmentRows.forEach(row => { const rowNumber = data.indexOf(row) + 2; // Get the actual row number (1-indexed, +1 for header) // Extract details directly from the sheet row using column indices const name = row[nameColumnIndex]; const yourTimestamp = row[yourTimestampColumnIndex]; // e.g., "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" const attendeeTzAbbrev = row[tzAbbrevColumnIndex]; // e.g., "CET" const attendeeTzFull = row[tzFullColumnIndex]; // e.g., "Central European Time" const phone = row[phoneColumnIndex]; // e.g., "+1-555-1212" const appointmentDateString = row[appointmentDateColumnIndex]; // e.g., "2025-04-29" // --- Format the subtask title for the evening list --- // Desired format: +1-555-1212 for Joe @ 4 PM EST THU May 22 // Need to convert YOUR time (derived from yourTimestamp and appointmentDateString) to ATTENDEE time let attendeeTimePart = 'Unknown Time'; let formattedAppointmentDatePart = 'Unknown Date'; // This will include Month Day and Day Abbrev try { // Attempt to parse the timestamp string from the sheet into a Date object in YOUR timezone. // The format of yourTimestamp is from the email "Event Date/Time:". // Example: "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" let meetingDateTimeInYourTZ = null; // Try parsing the email format "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" const emailFormatMatch = yourTimestamp.match(/^(\\d{1,2}:\\d{2}(?:am|pm)?)\\s\*-\\s\*(.\*?)\\s\*\\(/i); if (emailFormatMatch && emailFormatMatch[1] && emailFormatMatch[2]) { const timePart = emailFormatMatch[1]; // e.g., "10:30am" const datePart = emailFormatMatch[2].trim(); // e.g., "Thursday, April 24, 2025" const dateTimeStringInYourTZ = `${datePart} ${timePart}`; // e.g., "Thursday, April 24, 2025 10:30am" meetingDateTimeInYourTZ = new Date(dateTimeStringInYourTZ); Logger.log(`Attempted to parse email format timestamp for evening task: "${dateTimeStringInYourTZ}"`); } else { // Fallback: If the format is unexpected, try parsing as a standard date/time string // This might happen for manually added rows or transferred events if their timestamp format is different. // Combine the appointment date string with the timestamp string as a fallback const fallbackDateTimeString = `${appointmentDateString} ${yourTimestamp}`; meetingDateTimeInYourTZ = new Date(fallbackDateTimeString); Logger.log(`Attempted to parse fallback timestamp for evening task: "${fallbackDateTimeString}"`); } if (meetingDateTimeInYourTZ && !isNaN(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ.getTime())) { // Check if parsing was successful // Format the time in the Attendee's Full Time Zone // Use a format like "h:mm a" for time (e.g., "4:00 PM") // Use a format like "MMM dd" for Month and Day (e.g., "May 22") // Use a format like "EEE" for abbreviated Day (e.g., "THU") let targetTimeZone = attendeeTzFull || attendeeTzAbbrev || TIMEZONE; // Prefer full, then abbrev, fallback to script TZ try { // Format time in attendee's timezone attendeeTimePart = Utilities.formatDate(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ, targetTimeZone, "h:mm a"); // Format the date parts using the same target timezone formattedAppointmentDatePart = Utilities.formatDate(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ, targetTimeZone, "MMM dd"); const dayAbbrev = Utilities.formatDate(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ, targetTimeZone, "EEE").toUpperCase(); formattedAppointmentDatePart += `${dayAbbrev}`; // Add day abbreviation Logger.log(`Successfully formatted time and date in attendee TZ (${targetTimeZone}) for evening task: ${attendeeTimePart}, ${formattedAppointmentDatePart}`); } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error formatting date/time in attendee TZ (${targetTimeZone}) for evening task: ${e}. Falling back to raw timestamp.`); // Fallback: Use raw timestamp string if conversion fails attendeeTimePart = yourTimestamp; formattedAppointmentDatePart = ''; // No separate date part if timestamp is raw } } else { Logger.log(`Could not parse combined date/time string "${yourTimestamp}" into a valid Date object for evening task.`); // Fallback: Use raw timestamp string on parsing failure attendeeTimePart = yourTimestamp; formattedAppointmentDatePart = ''; // No separate date part if timestamp is raw } } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Unexpected error during time conversion or parsing for timestamp "${yourTimestamp}" for evening task: ${e}`); // Fallback: Use raw timestamp string on unexpected error attendeeTimePart = yourTimestamp; formattedAppointmentDatePart = ''; } // Assemble the final task title for the evening list const subtaskTitle = `${phone} for ${name} @ ${attendeeTimePart} ${attendeeTzAbbrev} ${formattedAppointmentDatePart}`; try { // Create the subtask under the parent task const subtask = Tasks.Tasks.insert({ title: subtaskTitle, parent: parentTask.id }, eveningTaskList.id); Logger.log(`Created subtask: "${subtask.title}" (ID: ${subtask.id})`); // Update the status and task IDs in the corresponding sheet row sheet.getRange(rowNumber, statusColumnIndex + 1).setValue('Evening Task Created'); // Update status to indicate task was created sheet.getRange(rowNumber, eveningTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue(subtask.id); sheet.getRange(rowNumber, eveningParentTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue(parentTask.id); } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error creating subtask for ${name}: ${e}`); // Update status to indicate failure sheet.getRange(rowNumber, statusColumnIndex + 1).setValue('Evening Task Creation Failed'); sheet.getRange(rowNumber, eveningTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue('ERROR'); // Mark ID columns too sheet.getRange(rowNumber, eveningParentTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue('ERROR'); } }); Logger.log('Evening batch task creation complete.'); } else { Logger.log(`No new appointments found for ${targetDayName} matching the target date and calendar check. No evening task created.`); } Logger.log('Finished processAppointmentsAndCreateEveningTask.'); } /\*\* \* Main function to check incomplete tasks from the previous evening AND transferred events \* that were logged to the sheet, and create morning follow-ups. \* Assumes Calendar check was performed by the evening script OR transferred events script. \* Formats the morning task title for easy manual texting, including time in ATTENDEE TZ. \* Refined time parsing based on "Event Date/Time" format. \* Should be triggered daily in the morning (around 06:00). \*/ function handleIncompleteMorningTasks() { Logger.log('Starting handleIncompleteMorningTasks (Refined Time Conversion)...'); const ss = SpreadsheetApp.openById(SPREADSHEET_ID); const sheet = ss.getSheetByName(SHEET_NAME); if (!sheet) { Logger.log(`Error: Sheet not found with name ${SHEET_NAME}. Aborting.`); return; } const data = sheet.getDataRange().getValues(); const header = data.shift(); // Remove header row // Find column indices dynamically based on header row const emailIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Email ID'); // Needed for sheet lookup const statusColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Status'); const eveningTaskIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Evening Task ID'); const eveningParentTaskIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Evening Parent Task ID'); const morningTaskIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Morning Task ID'); const morningParentTaskIdColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Morning Parent Task ID'); // Indices needed to build the morning task title and check appointment date const nameColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Name'); const yourTimestampColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Meeting Timestamp (Your TZ)'); // e.g., "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" or Calendar event time string const tzAbbrevColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Time Zone Abbrev'); // e.g., "CET" const tzFullColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Time Zone Full'); // e.g., "Central European Time" const phoneColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Contact Cell Phone'); // e.g., "+1-555-1212" const appointmentDateColumnIndex = header.indexOf('Appointment Date (Your TZ)'); // e.g., "2025-04-29" if (emailIdColumnIndex === -1 || statusColumnIndex === -1 || eveningTaskIdColumnIndex === -1 || eveningParentTaskIdColumnIndex === -1 || morningTaskIdColumnIndex === -1 || morningParentTaskIdColumnIndex === -1 || nameColumnIndex === -1 || yourTimestampColumnIndex === -1 || tzAbbrevColumnIndex === -1 || tzFullColumnIndex === -1 || phoneColumnIndex === -1 || appointmentDateColumnIndex === -1) { Logger.log("Error: Missing required columns in sheet header row. Cannot process incomplete tasks."); Logger.log("Required headers: 'Email ID', 'Meeting Timestamp (Your TZ)', 'Appointment Date (Your TZ)', 'Contact Name', 'Contact Cell Phone', 'Contact Time Zone Abbrev', 'Contact Time Zone Full', 'Contact Email', 'Status', 'Evening Task ID', 'Evening Parent Task ID', 'Morning Task ID', 'Morning Parent Task ID'"); return; } // Get the Evening and Morning Task Lists const eveningTaskList = getOrCreateTaskList(EVENING_TASK_LIST_NAME); const morningTaskList = getOrCreateTaskList(MORNING_TASK_LIST_NAME); // Get today's date and yesterday's date (for checking evening tasks from yesterday) const today = new Date(); const todayDayOfWeek = today.getDay(); // 0 for Sunday, 1 for Monday... const yesterday = new Date(today); yesterday.setDate(today.getDate() - 1); // Reset time to start of day for reliable comparison yesterday.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0); const yesterdayDateString = Utilities.formatDate(yesterday, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd"); // Get today's date string for processing transferred events logged today const todayDateString = Utilities.formatDate(today, TIMEZONE, "yyyy-MM-dd"); // --- Find incomplete tasks from yesterday's evening batch --- // These are tasks in the EVENING_TASK_LIST_NAME that are not completed // and whose corresponding sheet entry has yesterday's appointment date. const eveningParentTaskTitle = `Send Reminders for ${yesterdayDateString} Appointments`; let incompleteEveningTasks = []; try { const eveningTasks = Tasks.Tasks.list(eveningTaskList.id, { q: eveningParentTaskTitle }).items; if (eveningTasks && eveningTasks.length > 0) { const yesterdayParentTask = eveningTasks[0]; // Assuming the first match is correct Logger.log(`Found yesterday's evening parent task: "${yesterdayParentTask.title}". Fetching subtasks.`); const subtasks = Tasks.Tasks.list(eveningTaskList.id, { parent: yesterdayParentTask.id }).items; if (subtasks) { incompleteEveningTasks = subtasks.filter(subtask => subtask.status === 'needsAction'); Logger.log(`Found ${incompleteEveningTasks.length} incomplete tasks from yesterday's evening batch.`); } } else { Logger.log(`Could not find yesterday's evening parent task with title "${eveningParentTaskTitle}".`); } } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error fetching incomplete evening tasks: ${e}`); } // --- Find transferred events logged to sheet today that need morning tasks --- // These are rows in the sheet with status 'Transferred - Processed' and today's appointment date, // that don't have a Morning Task ID yet. const transferredRowsNeedingTask = data.filter(row => row[statusColumnIndex] === 'Transferred - Processed' && row[appointmentDateColumnIndex] === todayDateString && // Appointment date is today !row[morningTaskIdColumnIndex] // No morning task ID yet ); Logger.log(`Found ${transferredRowsNeedingTask.length} transferred events in sheet needing morning tasks.`); // --- Combine and Process Incomplete Tasks / Transferred Events --- let itemsToProcess = []; // Array of sheet row data to create morning tasks for // Add data from incomplete evening tasks (look up row in sheet) incompleteEveningTasks.forEach(subtask => { const row = data.find(r => r[eveningTaskIdColumnIndex] === subtask.id && r[appointmentDateColumnIndex] === yesterdayDateString // Ensure appointment date matches yesterday ); if (row) { itemsToProcess.push({ row: row, type: 'evening_incomplete' }); } else { Logger.log(`Could not find sheet row for incomplete Evening Task ID ${subtask.id} from yesterday. Skipping.`); } }); // Add data from transferred events needing tasks transferredRowsNeedingTask.forEach(row => { itemsToProcess.push({ row: row, type: 'transferred' }); }); Logger.log(`Total items to process for morning tasks: ${itemsToProcess.length}`); if (itemsToProcess.length === 0) { Logger.log("No items to process for morning tasks. Nothing to do."); return; } // Create the morning parent task if it doesn't exist yet for today let morningParentTask = null; const morningParentTaskTitle = `Follow up on ${todayDateString} Manual Reminders`; // Parent task for today's follow-ups try { const existingMorningTasks = Tasks.Tasks.list(morningTaskList.id, { q: morningParentTaskTitle }).items; if (existingMorningTasks && existingMorningTasks.length > 0) { morningParentTask = existingMorningTasks[0]; Logger.log(`Found existing morning parent task: "${morningParentTask.title}" (ID: ${morningParentTask.id})`); } else { // Create a new morning parent task for today const todayStartOfDay = new Date(today); todayStartOfDay.setHours(0,0,0,0); morningParentTask = Tasks.Tasks.insert({ title: morningParentTaskTitle, due: todayStartOfDay.toISOString(), // Parent task due today notes: "Reminder texts could not be scheduled automatically. Send these manually.", }, morningTaskList.id); Logger.log(`Created new morning parent task: "${morningParentTask.title}" (ID: ${morningParentTask.id})`); } } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error getting or creating morning parent task: ${e}`); return; // Cannot proceed without a parent task } // Process each item to create a morning subtask itemsToProcess.forEach(({ row, type }) => { const rowNumber = data.indexOf(row) + 2; // Get the actual row number // Extract details directly from the sheet row using column indices const name = row[nameColumnIndex]; const yourTimestamp = row[yourTimestampColumnIndex]; // e.g., "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" or Calendar event time string const attendeeTzAbbrev = row[tzAbbrevColumnIndex]; // e.g., "CET" const attendeeTzFull = row[tzFullColumnIndex]; // e.g., "Central European Time" const phone = row[phoneColumnIndex]; // e.g., "+1-555-1212" const appointmentDateString = row[appointmentDateColumnIndex]; // e.g., "2025-04-29" const appointmentDate = new Date(appointmentDateString); appointmentDate.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0); // Reset time for comparison // --- Determine the Due Date for the NEW Morning Task --- let morningTaskDueDate = new Date(today); // Default: due today morning morningTaskDueDate.setHours(8, 0, 0, 0); // Set to 08:00 today // Special case: If today is Saturday (6) AND the appointment is on Monday (1) // This logic applies if the item came from yesterday's evening batch (type === 'evening_incomplete') if (type === 'evening_incomplete' && todayDayOfWeek === 6 && appointmentDate.getDay() === 1) { Logger.log(`Special case: Incomplete task from Friday batch is for Monday appointment. Setting morning task due date to Monday.`); // Calculate Monday's date const mondayDate = new Date(today); mondayDate.setDate(today.getDate() + 2); // Add 2 days to Saturday to get Monday mondayDate.setHours(8, 0, 0, 0); // Set to 08:00 Monday morningTaskDueDate = mondayDate; } else { // For all other incomplete tasks and transferred events, the follow-up task is due today morning Logger.log(`Standard morning task due date (today) for item type: ${type}`); } const morningTaskDueDateISO = morningTaskDueDate.toISOString(); // --- Format the subtask title for the morning list --- // Desired format: +1-555-1212 for Joe @ 4 PM EST THU May 22 // Need to convert YOUR time (derived from yourTimestamp and appointmentDateString) to ATTENDEE time let attendeeTimePart = 'Unknown Time'; let formattedAppointmentDatePart = 'Unknown Date'; // This will include Month Day and Day Abbrev try { // Attempt to parse the timestamp string from the sheet into a Date object in YOUR timezone. // The format of yourTimestamp can vary (from email or calendar). // We need to be flexible here. let meetingDateTimeInYourTZ = null; // Try parsing the email format "10:30am - Thursday, April 24, 2025 (Bogota, Jamaica, Lima Time)" const emailFormatMatch = yourTimestamp.match(/^(\\d{1,2}:\\d{2}(?:am|pm)?)\\s\*-\\s\*(.\*?)\\s\*\\(/i); if (emailFormatMatch && emailFormatMatch[1] && emailFormatMatch[2]) { const timePart = emailFormatMatch[1]; // e.g., "10:30am" const datePart = emailFormatMatch[2].trim(); // e.g., "Thursday, April 24, 2025" const dateTimeStringInYourTZ = `${datePart} ${timePart}`; // e.g., "Thursday, April 24, 2025 10:30am" meetingDateTimeInYourTZ = new Date(dateTimeStringInYourTZ); Logger.log(`Attempted to parse email format timestamp for morning task: "${dateTimeStringInYourTZ}"`); } else { // Fallback: If the format is unexpected, try parsing as a standard date/time string // This might happen for manually added rows or transferred events if their timestamp format is different. // Combine the appointment date string with the timestamp string as a fallback const fallbackDateTimeString = `${appointmentDateString} ${yourTimestamp}`; meetingDateTimeInYourTZ = new Date(fallbackDateTimeString); Logger.log(`Attempted to parse fallback timestamp for morning task: "${fallbackDateTimeString}"`); } if (meetingDateTimeInYourTZ && !isNaN(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ.getTime())) { // Check if parsing was successful // Format the time in the Attendee's Full Time Zone // Use a format like "h:mm a" for time (e.g., "4:00 PM") // Use a format like "MMM dd" for Month and Day (e.g., "May 22") // Use a format like "EEE" for abbreviated Day (e.g., "THU") let targetTimeZone = attendeeTzFull || attendeeTzAbbrev || TIMEZONE; // Prefer full, then abbrev, fallback to script TZ try { // Format time in attendee's timezone attendeeTimePart = Utilities.formatDate(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ, targetTimeZone, "h:mm a"); // Format the date parts using the same target timezone formattedAppointmentDatePart = Utilities.formatDate(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ, targetTimeZone, "MMM dd"); const dayAbbrev = Utilities.formatDate(meetingDateTimeInYourTZ, targetTimeZone, "EEE").toUpperCase(); formattedAppointmentDatePart += `${dayAbbrev}`; // Add day abbreviation Logger.log(`Successfully formatted time and date in attendee TZ (${targetTimeZone}) for morning task: ${attendeeTimePart}, ${formattedAppointmentDatePart}`); } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error formatting date/time in attendee TZ (${targetTimeZone}) for morning task: ${e}. Falling back to raw timestamp.`); // Fallback: Use raw timestamp string if conversion fails attendeeTimePart = yourTimestamp; formattedAppointmentDatePart = ''; // No separate date part if timestamp is raw } } else { Logger.log(`Could not parse combined date/time string "${yourTimestamp}" into a valid Date object for morning task.`); // Fallback: Use raw timestamp string on parsing failure attendeeTimePart = yourTimestamp; formattedAppointmentDatePart = ''; // No separate date part if timestamp is raw } } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Unexpected error during time conversion or parsing for timestamp "${yourTimestamp}" for morning task: ${e}`); // Fallback: Use raw timestamp string on unexpected error attendeeTimePart = yourTimestamp; formattedAppointmentDatePart = ''; } // Assemble the final task title const morningSubtaskTitle = `${phone} for ${name} @ ${attendeeTimePart} ${attendeeTzAbbrev} ${formattedAppointmentDatePart}`; try { // Create the subtask under the morning parent task with the determined due date const morningSubtask = Tasks.Tasks.insert({ title: morningSubtaskTitle, parent: morningParentTask.id, due: morningTaskDueDateISO }, morningTaskList.id); Logger.log(`Created morning follow-up subtask: "${morningSubtask.title}" (ID: ${morningSubtask.id})" due ${morningTaskDueDateISO}`); // Update the status and Morning Task IDs in the sheet row sheet.getRange(rowNumber, statusColumnIndex + 1).setValue('Morning Task Created'); sheet.getRange(rowNumber, morningTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue(morningSubtask.id); sheet.getRange(rowNumber, morningParentTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue(morningParentTask.id); } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error creating morning subtask for ${name}: ${e}`); // Optionally, update status to indicate failure sheet.getRange(rowNumber, statusColumnIndex + 1).setValue('Morning Task Creation Failed'); sheet.getRange(rowNumber, morningTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue('ERROR'); // Mark ID columns too sheet.getRange(rowNumber, morningParentTaskIdColumnIndex + 1).setValue('ERROR'); } }); Logger.log('Finished handleIncompleteMorningTasks.'); } // --- Slack Reminder Functions --- /\*\* \* Sends a reminder message to a Slack channel via Incoming Webhook. \* Can send either an evening reminder or a morning follow-up reminder. \* @param {string} type - 'evening' or 'morning' to determine the message content. \*/ function sendSlackReminder(type) { Logger.log(`Attempting to send Slack reminder (${type})...`); // Make sure SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL constant is defined and updated at the top of your script! if (typeof SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL === 'undefined' || !SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL || SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL === 'PASTE_YOUR_SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL_HERE') { Logger.log('Slack Webhook URL is not configured correctly in the script. Skipping Slack notification.'); return; } const today = new Date(); const dateString = Utilities.formatDate(today, Session.getScriptTimeZone(), "EEEE, MMMM dd,yyyy"); // e.g., Monday, April 29, 2024 let messageText = ''; let reminderTitle = ''; if (type === 'evening') { // Message for the evening reminder reminderTitle = `🌙 Evening Reminder (${dateString})`; messageText = `It's time to check your Google Tasks "${EVENING_TASK_LIST_NAME}" list.\n\nPre-schedule reminder texts for tomorrow's appointments based on the tasks created.`; } else if (type === 'morning') { // Message for the morning follow-up reminder reminderTitle = `☀️ Morning Follow-up Reminder (${dateString})`; messageText = `Check your Google Tasks "${MORNING_TASK_LIST_NAME}" list for tasks that need manual follow-up today.\n\nThis includes appointments that couldn't be prescheduled last night, *and* any transferred events processed this morning.`; // Explicitly mention transferred events } else { Logger.log(`Invalid type "${type}" provided for sendSlackReminder. Skipping notification.`); return; // Exit if an invalid type is provided } // Construct the message payload for Slack const message = { text: `*${reminderTitle}*\n\n${messageText}`, // Optional: Customize the sender's name and icon in Slack (uncomment and modify if desired) // username: "Appointment Bot", // icon_emoji: ":calendar:", }; // Options for the HTTP POST request const options = { method: 'post', contentType: 'application/json', payload: JSON.stringify(message), muteHttpExceptions: true // Prevents script from stopping on HTTP errors (like a bad URL) }; try { // Send the message to Slack const response = UrlFetchApp.fetch(SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL, options); // Log success or error code from Slack Logger.log(`Slack message sent (${type}). Response code:` \+ response.getResponseCode()); // If response code is not 200, there might be an issue (e.g., invalid URL) if (response.getResponseCode() !== 200) { Logger.log('Slack API returned an error response: ' + response.getContentText()); Logger.log('Slack API response content: ' + response.getContentText()); // Log the error message from Slack } } catch (e) { Logger.log(`Error sending Slack message (${type}):` \+ e.toString()); } Logger.log(`Finished sending Slack reminder (${type}).`); } // --- Slack Reminder Wrapper Functions --- /\*\* \* Wrapper function to send the evening Slack reminder. \* Called by a time-driven trigger. \*/ function sendEveningSlackReminder() { sendSlackReminder('evening'); // Calls the main function with the 'evening' type } /\*\* \* Wrapper function to send the morning Slack follow-up reminder. \* Called by a time-driven trigger. \*/ function sendMorningSlackReminder() { sendSlackReminder('morning'); // Calls the main function with the 'morning' type }

## Q:

## A: 
💥 That’s **super helpful intel** — and confirms a key theory:

> The script is misaligning **date logic** during its **“look-ahead” scan**. Instead of checking _tomorrow’s_ appointments (e.g., Thursday), it’s re-processing _today’s_ (e.g., Wednesday) — which makes it miss your actual upcoming calls.

Combine that with:

*   It’s **still filtering by `unread`** even though we intended not to
    
*   Snoozed or previously opened Gmail threads aren’t being re-parsed
    
*   And it’s using **string parsing** on natural-language time data instead of ISO-standard timestamps (fragile af)

*   Last night’s trigger run
    
*   This morning’s follow-up

Once I see those, I’ll:

*   Confirm where the script breaks or skips over valid data
    
*   Show you exactly what’s misfiring and where in the code
    
*   Patch it for **label + date accuracy** and more reliable extraction

## A: 
YES. This is exactly the kind of full-context snapshot I needed.

### 🧠 TL;DR: I’ve got everything I need to debug this sucker.

Here’s what your screenshot + email sample confirm beyond any doubt:

* * *

### 🔥 1. THE BUG:

Your current script is **failing the date logic.**

*   **Log says:** `Found and processed 0 new appointment emails for Thursday`
    
*   **Reality:** You had **5 Thursday appointments** (including Cristina’s at 11:00am)
    
*   Why? Because the parser is extracting the date from the _timestamp string in the email_ using this regex:
    
    JavaScript
    
    ```
    const datePartMatch = details.yourTimestamp.match(/-\s*(.*?)\s*\(/);
    ```
    
    — but that returns `"Thursday, May 1, 2025"`  
    Which `new Date()` **fails to parse in Apps Script** (returns `Invalid Date`)
    

* * *

### 🪓 2. THE FIX:

We’ll replace fragile regex parsing + fuzzy `Date` conversions with:

*   **Structured, hard-coded parsing of the Calendly timestamp format** (e.g. `"11:00am - Thursday, May 1, 2025 (Time Zone)"`)
    
*   Or even better:
    
    *   Use the **actual calendar event date** (from the confirmation email) _after validating it's tied to a real Calendar event_
        
    *   That way, if parsing fails but the event exists — we still win
        

* * *

### 🧹 3. OTHER MINOR ISSUES TO CLEAN UP:

*   `message.isUnread()` should be **removed entirely**
    
*   You already **trust the label**, and snoozed or reopened messages might show as "read"
    
*   Also that morning task log error (`TypeError: Cannot read properties of undefined (reading 'list')`) means Tasks API didn’t fire — could be a temporary auth issue or quota hit. We'll defensively code around it.
    

* * *

### ✅ WHAT HAPPENS NEXT:

I’m rewriting the core of the `processAppointmentsAndCreateEveningTask()` function to:

*   Use label only (ignore unread)
    
*   Strip and normalize the Calendly date string with robust fallback
    
*   Verify the extracted date **matches the appointment date in Calendar**
    
*   Skip parsing errors, but **log which message failed and why** (new column?)
    

And I’ll confirm the other helper functions are still solid once the update’s done.

💬 Let me know if you want:

*   A **fully cleaned-up version of the entire script**
    
*   Or just the patched section with **instructions on where to replace**
    

Ready when you say “GO.”
