## Q: 
It's Thursday at 7 PM right now, you should be looking for Friday calls

## A: 
💥 Nailed it — you're exactly right.

The script is working _as coded_, but the logic in `getTargetDate()` says:

JavaScript

```
const delta = dow === 5 ? 3 : 1; // If Friday, skip to Monday
```

You're running it **on Thursday night**, but the code is still pointing to **Friday** as the _next_ day to process.

### 🔧 Fix: Change `getTargetDate()` to look ahead properly based on **current day**, not assuming it’s running in the morning

If you want **Thursday night runs** to prep for **Friday** (not Monday), then update the logic to this:

JavaScript

```
function getTargetDate(today = new Date()) {  const dow = today.getDay();  // If Thursday (4), look 1 day ahead → Friday  // If Friday (5), look 3 days ahead → Monday  const delta = dow === 5 ? 3 : 1;  const target = new Date(today);  target.setDate(today.getDate() + delta);  target.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0);  return target;}
```

But **your existing code already does this** — and it **should** have pulled for Friday just fine.

### 🤔 So here’s what _really_ happened:

Your Thursday evening run looked for **emails labeled for Friday**:

JavaScript

```
label:"5 - Friday 🎉"
```

And unless **Cristina’s email** had _that label_ (`5 - Friday 🎉`), the script wouldn’t touch it.

You said her booking was for **Thursday at 11:00am**, which means:

*   It was **missed** on **Wednesday night**, when the label would’ve been:
    
    Code
    
    ```
    4 - Thursday 🥤
    ```
    

* * *

### ✅ What to do now:

1.  Manually label Cristina’s email with `5 - Friday 🎉` in Gmail.
    
2.  Re-run `pullBookingsToSheet()`.
    
3.  It should show up in your Google Sheet now — and we can continue to Phase 2 (task creation).
    

Want me to tweak the code to make this more _date-based_ than label-based (e.g. only pulling emails **with a date that matches the booking day**) instead of relying on Gmail labels?

```
function pullCalendarBookingsToSheet() {  const [start, end] = getDateRangeForNextDay();  const calendar = CalendarApp.getCalendarById(CALENDAR_ID);  const events = calendar.getEvents(start, end);  console.log(`🔍 Checking events from ${start.toISOString()} to ${end.toISOString()}`);  console.log(`📅 Found ${events.length} total event(s) on the calendar.`);  let count = 0;  for (const event of events) {    const title = event.getTitle();    console.log(`👉 Event found: "${title}"`);    if (!title.includes('Onboarding')) {      console.log(`⛔ Skipped: "${title}" — does not contain "Onboarding"`);      continue;    }    const details = parseEventDetails(event);    console.log(`✅ Parsed:`, details);    if (details.name && details.timestamp) {      logCalendarEventToSheet(details);      count++;    }  }  console.log(`✅ Calendar scan complete. ${count} event(s) logged for ${Utilities.formatDate(start, TIMEZONE, 'EEEE')}.`);}
```

* * *

### Why this matters:

If that prints `📅 Found 0 event(s)` → the script is NOT looking at the correct calendar.  
If it prints events but skips them → the filter or parsing logic is off.

give me the entire code to put into the editor if you're asking me to change it please

## A: 
```javascript
// Booking Reminder Rebuild v2.1 — Calendar-Based Debug Mode
// Phase 1: Google Calendar → Sheet (Gmail skipped entirely for sanity's sake)

const SPREADSHEET_ID = '1bfqAQtN97bY-dEguPq80kh-fabB5LEq2Xhnsc-FHkks';
const SHEET_NAME = 'Bookings';
const TIMEZONE = Session.getScriptTimeZone();
const CALENDAR_ID = 'primary'; // Change this if pulling from another calendar

function getNextDayDate(today = new Date()) {
const next = new Date(today);
next.setDate(today.getDate() + 1);
next.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0);
return next;
}

function getDateRangeForNextDay() {
const start = getNextDayDate();
const end = new Date(start);
end.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);
return [start, end];
}

function parseEventDetails(event) {
const description = event.getDescription();
const emailMatch = description.match(/Invitee Email:\s*(\S+)/);
const phoneMatch = description.match(/Phone Number:\s*(\+?[\d\s]+)/);
const timezoneMatch = description.match(/Invitee Time Zone:\s*(.*)/);

return {
name: event.getTitle().replace(/^(.*?) - /, '').trim(),
timestamp: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm'),
date: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd'),
email: emailMatch ? emailMatch[1].trim() : '',
phone: phoneMatch ? phoneMatch[1].trim() : '',
tzFull: timezoneMatch ? timezoneMatch[1].trim() : '',
tzAbbrev: '', // Optional: logic to convert tzFull to abbrev if needed
```

*   ✅ if they're parsed and logged.
    

Send me the full log output right after running if it still doesn't write to your Sheet. Ready when you are.

Here's your results: 7:47:17 PM Notice Execution started 7:47:17 PM Info 🔍 Checking events from 2025-05-02T05:00:00.000Z to 2025-05-03T05:00:00.000Z 7:47:17 PM Info 📅 Found 4 total event(s) on the calendar. 7:47:17 PM Info 👉 Event found: "Elias Gerner's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" 7:47:17 PM Info ⛔ Skipped: "Elias Gerner's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" — does not contain "Onboarding" 7:47:17 PM Info 👉 Event found: "Daniel Kagan's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" 7:47:17 PM Info ⛔ Skipped: "Daniel Kagan's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" — does not contain "Onboarding" 7:47:17 PM Info 👉 Event found: "Betty Laur's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" 7:47:17 PM Info ⛔ Skipped: "Betty Laur's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" — does not contain "Onboarding" 7:47:17 PM Info 👉 Event found: "argueta's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" 7:47:17 PM Info ⛔ Skipped: "argueta's POPPY AI ONBOARDING with Patty Woods" — does not contain "Onboarding" 7:47:17 PM Info ✅ Calendar scan complete. 0 event(s) logged for Friday. 7:47:17 PM Notice Execution completed

## A: 
Perfect diagnosis — and you're absolutely right. The code is currently doing a **case-sensitive** check for `"Onboarding"` in the event title. Since your titles are in **ALL CAPS ("ONBOARDING")**, the condition fails and nothing gets logged.

Let’s fix that now by making the match **case-insensitive** ✅

### 🔧 Here’s the updated `pullCalendarBookingsToSheet()` function with a lowercase comparison:

JavaScript

```
function pullCalendarBookingsToSheet() {  const [start, end] = getDateRangeForNextDay();  const calendar = CalendarApp.getCalendarById(CALENDAR_ID);  const events = calendar.getEvents(start, end);  console.log(`🔍 Checking events from ${start.toISOString()} to ${end.toISOString()}`);  console.log(`📅 Found ${events.length} total event(s) on the calendar.`);  let count = 0;  for (const event of events) {    const title = event.getTitle();    console.log(`👉 Event found: "${title}"`);    // Case-insensitive match    if (!title.toLowerCase().includes('onboarding')) {      console.log(`⛔ Skipped: "${title}" — does not include 'onboarding' (case-insensitive)`);      continue;    }    const details = parseEventDetails(event);    console.log(`✅ Parsed:`, details);    if (details.name && details.timestamp) {      logCalendarEventToSheet(details);      count++;    }  }  console.log(`✅ Calendar scan complete. ${count} event(s) logged for ${Utilities.formatDate(start, TIMEZONE, 'EEEE')}.`);}
```

## Q: 
Before I update my script again, today is now Friday, May 2, 2025, and we'll want to do the look ahead for what's on the Calendar on Monday, May 5, 2025. Do you need to do anything to the script right now so I can add it and test it so it jumps to the right WEEKDAY look ahead date?

## A: 
Yes — we need to **temporarily adjust the script** so it targets **Monday, May 5** instead of blindly grabbing "tomorrow."

Here’s how to modify that:

* * *

### 🔁 REPLACE this function:

JavaScript

```
function getDateRangeForNextDay() {  const start = getNextDayDate();  const end = new Date(start);  end.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);  return [start, end];}
```

* * *

### ✅ WITH this version that looks ahead to Monday:

JavaScript

```
function getDateRangeForNextDay() {  const today = new Date();  const dayOfWeek = today.getDay(); // Sunday = 0, Monday = 1, ..., Saturday = 6  const daysUntilMonday = (8 - dayOfWeek) % 7 || 7;  const start = new Date(today);  start.setDate(today.getDate() + daysUntilMonday);  start.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0);  const end = new Date(start);  end.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);  return [start, end];}
```

* * *

### 💡 What it does:

*   Today is Friday (`getDay() === 5`)
    
*   That means `daysUntilMonday` becomes `3`
    
*   Script will now check events **from midnight Monday → midnight Tuesday**
    

You can swap this back to a dynamic "next-day" function once we confirm this works with your upcoming Monday bookings.

Let me know if you want a toggle-based option for easier future testing. Ready to run when you are.

### ✅ Booking Reminder Rebuild v2.2 — Calendar Lookahead to Monday

JavaScript

```
// Booking Reminder Rebuild v2.2 — Lookahead to Monday Only// Phase 1: Google Calendar → Sheet (Gmail skipped entirely)const SPREADSHEET_ID = '1bfqAQtN97bY-dEguPq80kh-fabB5LEq2Xhnsc-FHkks';const SHEET_NAME = 'Bookings';const TIMEZONE = Session.getScriptTimeZone();const CALENDAR_ID = 'primary'; // If using a different calendar, swap thisfunction getDateRangeForNextDay() {  const today = new Date();  const dayOfWeek = today.getDay(); // Sunday = 0, Monday = 1, ..., Saturday = 6  const daysUntilMonday = (8 - dayOfWeek) % 7 || 7;  const start = new Date(today);  start.setDate(today.getDate() + daysUntilMonday);  start.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0);  const end = new Date(start);  end.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);  return [start, end];}function parseEventDetails(event) {  const description = event.getDescription();  const emailMatch = description.match(/Invitee Email:\s*(\S+)/);  const phoneMatch = description.match(/Phone Number:\s*(\+?[\d\s]+)/);  const timezoneMatch = description.match(/Invitee Time Zone:\s*(.*)/);  return {    name: event.getTitle().replace(/^(.*?) - /, '').trim(),    timestamp: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm'),    date: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd'),    email: emailMatch ? emailMatch[1].trim() : '',    phone: phoneMatch ? phoneMatch[1].trim() : '',    tzFull: timezoneMatch ? timezoneMatch[1].trim() : '',    tzAbbrev: '', // Optional: You can add logic to convert to timezone abbreviations  };}function logCalendarEventToSheet(eventData) {  const ss = SpreadsheetApp.openById(SPREADSHEET_ID);  const sheet = ss.getSheetByName(SHEET_NAME);  if (!sheet) return;  sheet.appendRow([    `cal-${Date.now()}`,    eventData.timestamp,    eventData.date,    eventData.name,    eventData.phone,    eventData.tzAbbrev,    eventData.tzFull,    eventData.email,    'Logged from Google Calendar',    '', '', '', ''  ]);}function pullCalendarBookingsToSheet() {  const [start, end] = getDateRangeForNextDay();  const calendar = CalendarApp.getCalendarById(CALENDAR_ID);  const events = calendar.getEvents(start, end);  console.log(`🔍 Checking events from ${start.toISOString()} to ${end.toISOString()}`);  console.log(`📅 Found ${events.length} total event(s) on the calendar.`);  let count = 0;  for (const event of events) {    const title = event.getTitle();    console.log(`👉 Event found: "${title}"`);    if (!title.includes('Onboarding')) {      console.log(`⛔ Skipped: "${title}" — does not contain "Onboarding"`);      continue;    }    const details = parseEventDetails(event);    console.log(`✅ Parsed:`, details);    if (details.name && details.timestamp) {      logCalendarEventToSheet(details);      count++;    }  }  console.log(`✅ Calendar scan complete. ${count} event(s) logged for ${Utilities.formatDate(start, TIMEZONE, 'EEEE')}.`);}
```

*   🔁 Flip between “only run this once” and “safe to run repeatedly”

### ✅ Fixed + Test-Ready Script (v2.3 with Case Fix + Toggle)

JavaScript

```
// Booking Reminder Rebuild v2.3 — Case-insensitive match + TEST_MODE toggleconst SPREADSHEET_ID = '1bfqAQtN97bY-dEguPq80kh-fabB5LEq2Xhnsc-FHkks';const SHEET_NAME = 'Bookings';const TIMEZONE = Session.getScriptTimeZone();const CALENDAR_ID = 'primary';const TEST_MODE = false; // 👉 set to true to simulate run without appending rowsfunction getDateRangeForNextMonday() {  const today = new Date();  const dayOfWeek = today.getDay(); // Sunday = 0 ... Saturday = 6  const daysUntilMonday = (8 - dayOfWeek) % 7 || 7;  const start = new Date(today);  start.setDate(today.getDate() + daysUntilMonday);  start.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0);  const end = new Date(start);  end.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);  return [start, end];}function parseEventDetails(event) {  const description = event.getDescription();  const emailMatch = description.match(/Invitee Email:\s*(\S+)/);  const phoneMatch = description.match(/Phone Number:\s*(\+?[\d\s]+)/);  const timezoneMatch = description.match(/Invitee Time Zone:\s*(.*)/);  return {    name: event.getTitle().replace(/^(.*?) - /, '').trim(),    timestamp: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm'),    date: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd'),    email: emailMatch ? emailMatch[1].trim() : '',    phone: phoneMatch ? phoneMatch[1].trim() : '',    tzFull: timezoneMatch ? timezoneMatch[1].trim() : '',    tzAbbrev: '',  };}function logCalendarEventToSheet(eventData) {  if (TEST_MODE) {    console.log(`🧪 TEST_MODE enabled. Would log event: ${eventData.name}`);    return;  }  const ss = SpreadsheetApp.openById(SPREADSHEET_ID);  const sheet = ss.getSheetByName(SHEET_NAME);  if (!sheet) return;  sheet.appendRow([    `cal-${Date.now()}`,    eventData.timestamp,    eventData.date,    eventData.name,    eventData.phone,    eventData.tzAbbrev,    eventData.tzFull,    eventData.email,    'Logged from Google Calendar',    '', '', '', ''  ]);}function pullCalendarBookingsToSheet() {  const [start, end] = getDateRangeForNextMonday();  const calendar = CalendarApp.getCalendarById(CALENDAR_ID);  const events = calendar.getEvents(start, end);  console.log(`🔍 Checking events from ${start.toISOString()} to ${end.toISOString()}`);  console.log(`📅 Found ${events.length} total event(s) on the calendar.`);  let count = 0;  for (const event of events) {    const title = event.getTitle();    console.log(`👉 Event found: "${title}"`);    if (!title.toLowerCase().includes('onboarding')) {      console.log(`⛔ Skipped: "${title}" — does not contain "onboarding" (case-insensitive)`);      continue;    }    const details = parseEventDetails(event);    console.log(`✅ Parsed:`, details);    if (details.name && details.timestamp) {      logCalendarEventToSheet(details);      count++;    }  }  const dayName = Utilities.formatDate(start, TIMEZONE, 'EEEE');  console.log(`✅ Calendar scan complete. ${count} event(s) logged for ${dayName}.`);}
```

* * *

### 🚦How to Use the `TEST_MODE`

*   Set `const TEST_MODE = true` to **preview** logs without writing to the sheet.
    
*   Set it to `false` to **actually log** data into your Google Sheet.
    
*   Useful when debugging regex, title formats, or working with multiple rounds of Calendar data.

* * *

### 🧪 **What the `TEST_MODE` Toggle Does**

Inside the script:

JavaScript

```
const TEST_MODE = false; // 👈 flip this to true for safe testing
```

#### ✅ When `TEST_MODE = true`:

*   The script **runs everything** (calendar scan, parsing, filtering).
    
*   BUT it **doesn’t write to the sheet.**
    
*   Instead, it logs what _would_ have been written:
    
    Code
    
    ```
    🧪 TEST_MODE enabled. Would log event: Elias Gerner
    ```
    

**Why it rocks:**

*   You can test without cluttering your sheet.
    
*   Useful if you’re debugging logic, regex, time zone issues, or edge cases.
    
*   Safer for iterating when multiple people are looking at the sheet or when a team is using it live.

## Q:

## A: 
In most coding and data workflows, `yyyy-mm-dd` is standard because:

*   **Sorting:** It sorts chronologically by default.
    
*   **ISO 8601 compliant:** It’s the international standard.
    
*   **Unambiguous:** Avoids confusion between U.S. (mm-dd-yyyy) and European (dd-mm-yyyy) formats.
    

That said, for your **human-friendly, creative planning doc**, we can switch to `mm-dd-yyyy` without breaking a thing. I’ll update the **"Deliver or Defer By"** field in the Google Doc to use that format now.

### **Micro-Mod Evergreen Optimization Plan**

**1\. Product-ize the Setup**

*   Make it **Google Calendar + Google Sheets only** (no Zapier, no API keys, no Gmail parsing unless absolutely necessary)

*   Strip out anything requiring unique filters (like “only grab onboarding calls with specific casing”)

Solid catch. Here’s the situation:

### 🧠 Diagnosis Summary:

1.  **Wrong Date Range Pulled**  
    Yep—you’re right. I left in a **hardcoded test date (May 12)** instead of the expected “tomorrow” logic. That’s why you're seeing data from next week, not May 7.

## A: 
Alright, let’s do this! ✅ Today is **May 6**, so we’re pulling **May 7** appointments. Here’s the updated and fixed **Google Apps Script** code that:

*   Looks up events for **tomorrow** (May 7, 2025),
    
*   Properly extracts the **invitee email**, **phone**, and **timezone** from the Calendar **event description**, and
    
*   Logs them in the correct columns in your existing Google Sheet structure.
    

### ✅ Copy & Paste the Full Script Below into Your Script Editor:

JavaScript

```
// Booking Reminder Rebuild v3.0 — Calendar-Based Parse// Phase 1: Calendar → Sheet (Future-Aware, Live Booking Events)const SPREADSHEET_ID = '1bfqAQtN97bY-dEguPq80kh-fabB5LEq2Xhnsc-FHkks';const SHEET_NAME = 'Bookings';const TIMEZONE = Session.getScriptTimeZone();const CALENDAR_ID = 'primary';// -- UTILITIES --function getTomorrowRange() {  const start = new Date();  start.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);  start.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0);  const end = new Date(start);  end.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);  return [start, end];}function extractFromDescription(text, label) {  const regex = new RegExp(label + '\\s*[:：]+\\s*(.+)', 'i');  const match = text.match(regex);  return match ? match[1].trim() : '';}function parseCalendarEvent(event) {  const description = event.getDescription() || '';  const guests = event.getGuestList();  const invitee = guests.find(g => !g.getEmail().includes('@getpoppy.ai'));  const email = invitee ? invitee.getEmail() : '';  const phone = extractFromDescription(description, 'Phone Number');  const timezone = extractFromDescription(description, 'Invitee Time Zone');  return {    id: `cal-${Date.now()}`,    timestamp: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm'),    date: Utilities.formatDate(event.getStartTime(), TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd'),    contactName: event.getTitle(),    phone: phone,    tzFull: timezone,    tzAbbrev: '', // Future logic optional    email: email  };}function logEventToSheet(entry) {  const ss = SpreadsheetApp.openById(SPREADSHEET_ID);  const sheet = ss.getSheetByName(SHEET_NAME);  if (!sheet) return;  sheet.appendRow([    entry.id,    entry.timestamp,    entry.date,    entry.contactName,    entry.phone,    entry.tzAbbrev,    entry.tzFull,    entry.email,    'Logged from Calendar',    '', '', '', ''  ]);}function pullTomorrowBookingsToSheet() {  const [start, end] = getTomorrowRange();  const calendar = CalendarApp.getCalendarById(CALENDAR_ID);  const events = calendar.getEvents(start, end);  console.log(`🔍 Scanning events from ${start.toISOString()} to ${end.toISOString()}`);  console.log(`📅 Found ${events.length} event(s).`);  let count = 0;  for (const event of events) {    const title = event.getTitle();    if (!title.toLowerCase().includes('onboarding')) {      console.log(`⛔ Skipped: ${title}`);      continue;    }    const parsed = parseCalendarEvent(event);    if (parsed.email && parsed.timestamp) {      logEventToSheet(parsed);      count++;    }  }  console.log(`✅ Done. ${count} onboarding event(s) logged for tomorrow.`);}
```

* * *

### ✅ What’s Fixed:

*   Correct day: Tomorrow = May 7 ✅
    
*   Filters “Onboarding” case-insensitively ✅
    
*   Pulls attendee name, phone, email, time zone from event details ✅
    
*   Logs in the right columns in the sheet ✅

    *   Cell phone (if present)

Here’s the full, fixed Google Apps Script that:

✅ Pulls only **tomorrow’s** events  
✅ Extracts the attendee name correctly  
✅ Grabs phone, email, full time zone, and calculates the **abbreviation**  
✅ Logs everything cleanly into your sheet with your preferred columns

* * *

### ✅ Copy and Paste This Entire Code Block into Your Script Editor

JavaScript

```
// Booking Reminder Rebuild v2.4 — Calendar-Based with Clean Parsing// Pulls events for tomorrow and logs them with proper formattingconst SPREADSHEET_ID = '1bfqAQtN97bY-dEguPq80kh-fabB5LEq2Xhnsc-FHkks';const SHEET_NAME = 'Bookings';const TIMEZONE = Session.getScriptTimeZone();const CALENDAR_ID = 'primary';function getTomorrowRange() {  const start = new Date();  start.setDate(start.getDate() + 1);  start.setHours(0, 0, 0, 0);  const end = new Date(start);  end.setDate(end.getDate() + 1);  return [start, end];}function getTimeZoneAbbrev(timeZoneId, date = new Date()) {  const options = { timeZone: timeZoneId, timeZoneName: 'short' };  const parts = new Intl.DateTimeFormat('en-US', options).formatToParts(date);  const abbrev = parts.find(part => part.type === 'timeZoneName');  return abbrev ? abbrev.value : '';}function extractAttendeeName(title) {  const match = title.match(/^(.+?)'s .*ONBOARDING/i);  return match ? match[1].trim() : '';}function parseEvent(event) {  const desc = event.getDescription();  const emailMatch = desc.match(/([a-zA-Z0-9._%+-]+@[a-zA-Z0-9.-]+\.[a-zA-Z]+)/);  const phoneMatch = desc.match(/Phone Number[^:]*:*\s*(\+?[\d\-()\s]+)/i);  const tzMatch = desc.match(/(?:Invitee Time Zone|Time Zone):\s*([\w\s/]+)\b/);  const attendeeEmail = emailMatch ? emailMatch[1].trim() : '';  const attendeePhone = phoneMatch ? phoneMatch[1].trim() : '';  const attendeeTZ = tzMatch ? tzMatch[1].trim() : '';  const start = event.getStartTime();  const localTimestamp = Utilities.formatDate(start, TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm');  const localDate = Utilities.formatDate(start, TIMEZONE, 'yyyy-MM-dd');  const tzAbbrev = attendeeTZ ? getTimeZoneAbbrev(attendeeTZ, start) : '';  return {    id: 'cal-' + Date.now() + Math.floor(Math.random() * 1000),    timestamp: localTimestamp,    date: localDate,    contactName: extractAttendeeName(event.getTitle()),    phone: attendeePhone || '#ERROR!',    tzAbbrev: tzAbbrev || '',    tzFull: attendeeTZ || '',    email: attendeeEmail || '',    status: 'Logged from Calendar',  };}function logToSheet(eventData) {  const sheet = SpreadsheetApp.openById(SPREADSHEET_ID).getSheetByName(SHEET_NAME);  sheet.appendRow([    eventData.id,    eventData.timestamp,    eventData.date,    eventData.contactName,    eventData.phone,    eventData.tzAbbrev,    eventData.tzFull,    eventData.email,    eventData.status,    '', '', '', '' // Task ID columns (optional)  ]);}function pullTomorrowCalendarBookings() {  const [start, end] = getTomorrowRange();  const calendar = CalendarApp.getCalendarById(CALENDAR_ID);  const events = calendar.getEvents(start, end);  console.log(`🔍 Scanning for events from ${start} to ${end}`);  console.log(`📅 Found ${events.length} events`);  let count = 0;  for (const event of events) {    const title = event.getTitle();    console.log(`🧐 Checking event: "${title}"`);    if (!title.includes('ONBOARDING')) {      console.log(`⏭️ Skipped — doesn't match onboarding format`);      continue;    }    const data = parseEvent(event);    logToSheet(data);    count++;  }  console.log(`✅ Logged ${count} onboarding event(s) for ${Utilities.formatDate(start, TIMEZONE, 'EEEE')}`);}
```

* * *

### ✅ To Run It Now:

1.  Open **Apps Script**.
    
2.  Paste the entire code above.
    
3.  Save.
    
4.  From the function dropdown, select `pullTomorrowCalendarBookings`.
    
5.  Hit **Run**.

Need to know what the conversion is to their TZ from the time it’s stated on my cal/my TZ. If I say they have a call at 10 AM CST and they’re on CET, they want to know the call is at 4 PM CET

## A: 
Got it — this is **absolutely critical** and here's how we handle it:

* * *

### **The Key Conversion You Need:**

Your Google Calendar shows **your local time** (e.g. `10:00 AM CST`), but your clients need to receive:

> **"Your call is at 4:00 PM CET."**

* * *

### **How We Solve This (No More Guesswork):**

#### **1. Use the Attendee’s Time Zone from Calendly**

*   Calendly **includes the invitee’s actual time zone** in every booking
    
*   We pull this via the **Calendly API** (via **Make**)
    
*   This gives us their full timezone string (e.g. `Europe/Berlin`)
    

#### **2. Use Make’s Formatter to Convert Timezones**

*   Make’s **Date/Time Formatter** lets us:
    
    *   Input: `2025-05-07 10:00 AM` (your CST time)
        
    *   Convert to: `Europe/Berlin`
        
    *   Output: `2025-05-07 17:00` (5:00 PM CET)
        

#### **3. Output to Google Sheets or Google Tasks**

*   We’ll write both versions:
    
    *   **Your Local Time** (for you)
        
    *   **Their Time + Abbreviation** (for them)
        
*   That goes in the **Google Sheet AND the final text message** you send
    

* * *

### **Example Subtask in Google Tasks:**

> `Text Evan Dorfman (5:00 PM CET / 10:00 AM Your Time) at +1 312-375-8876`

* * *

### **You're Covered**

This removes 100% of timezone math.  
You're just confirming, texting, and checking it off. No calendar flipping. No mental conversion.

## Q: 
What about the Slack reminder as a batch task like we originally had going off at a set time? And also, what about the secondary fallback from calls that get transferred to me via Google Calendar after being booked to a different specialist on Calendly? How are those gonna be handled

## A: 
Alright, Captain No-Bullshit—here’s the straight-up breakdown:

* * *

### **1. SLACK REMINDER AS A BATCH (Not Per Event)**

Instead of a separate Slack message per booking, you get **one consolidated Slack reminder**, like:

> **Today’s Reminder: Text Your Poppy Peeps**
> 
> *   Elias Gerner — 4:00 PM CET | +49 1516 8169923
>     
> *   Justin Schaeffer — 10:00 AM PST | +1 415 000 1234
>     
> *   Betty Laur — 3:00 PM EST | +1 305 999 5678
>     
> 
> **Paste-ready text examples included below each.**

**This hits at a set time (like 7:30 AM daily)** and consolidates all of them for you to handle at once on your phone.

**In Make**, you’d:

*   Pull all Sheet rows for today’s date
    
*   Format them into one message
    
*   Send to Slack at fixed time
    

* * *

### **2. SECONDARY FALLBACK: TRANSFERRED EVENTS FROM OTHER SPECIALISTS**

This is a sneaky one but here's how we nail it:

**Assumption:** When a booking is transferred to your calendar via Calendly’s routing or manual reschedule, it **still shows up on your Google Calendar** (because the email address is assigned to you).

**So we do this:**

*   **Scan your calendar ONLY for events titled "ONBOARDING"**
    
*   **Ignore who originally booked it or which calendar it came from**
    
*   **Just parse whatever’s on YOUR Google Calendar for tomorrow**
    

**If it’s in your cal, it’s yours to prep for. Period.**

**Bonus Filter:** You can optionally scan the event description or attendee list to ensure **you’re one of the attendees**, to filter out duplicates or ghost reassignments.

* * *

### TL;DR:

*   Slack Reminder = batch summary with all text info, hits once a day
    
*   Fallback events = parsed same way as any other, as long as they’re on your calendar
    
*   No extra logic needed unless you’re sharing a calendar or getting ghost events from past owners
    

Want me to prep the scenario shell with this logic built-in so you can plug it into Make tomorrow and test it?

## Q:

## A: 
Yes — you _can_ get Slack reminders for these, but not natively through ChatGPT. Here's how to do it with the least friction:

### Option 1: **Use Slack’s built-in `/remind` command**

*   Open any Slack DM or channel (even your own DM to yourself)
    
*   Type:
    
    Code
    
    ```
    /remind me every Friday at 8:30am to “Prep for Weekly ☎️ → 🌸⚡️⬆️ Las 3 Chiquitas”
    ```
    
    and hit enter.
    
*   Do the same for your monthly reminder:
    
    Code
    
    ```
    /remind me on the 23rd of every month at 1:00pm to “Prep your 🧾🌸 for the 24th”
    ```
    

This works _instantly_ and doesn’t require Zapier or any other integration.

* * *

### Option 2: **Automate via Google Calendar + Make (or Zapier) → Slack**

If you're already automating Google Calendar tasks (like we’re doing for the booking parser), I can:

*   Add these reminders to a specific calendar
    
*   Then fire a Make automation that posts into your Slack DM with the reminder content at the right time.
    

Want to go with Option 1 for simplicity or loop in Option 2 later with your calendar system?

## Q: 
What I’m saying is, ChatGPT reminds me via email. What if instead when that email hits my inbox, I set up a Gmail filter so I don’t have to see it clutter up my email, apply a filter, and that filter triggers a slack message

## A: 
Yes — **brilliant workaround**. Here’s how to set it up clean:

* * *

### **Step 1: Create a Gmail Filter**

1.  Wait for a ChatGPT reminder email to land in your inbox (you’ll need at least one to use as the template).
    
2.  Open it, click the 3 dots → **Filter messages like these**
    
3.  Filter by:
    
    *   `From: no-reply@openai.com`
        
    *   `Subject: Reminder:` (or whatever consistent prefix ChatGPT uses)
        
4.  Click **Create filter**
    
5.  Choose:
    
    *   **Skip the Inbox (Archive it)**
        
    *   **Apply label:** `ChatGPT Reminders` (create one if needed)
        
    *   **Never send it to Spam**
        

* * *

### **Step 2: Use Zapier or Make to Watch for That Label**

**Zapier:**

*   **Trigger:** New email in Gmail with label `ChatGPT Reminders`
    
*   **Action:** Send Slack message to you with the subject or snippet of the email
    

**Make (Integromat):**

*   **Gmail module:** Watch emails with label `ChatGPT Reminders`
    
*   **Slack module:** Send message to channel or user
    

* * *

### **Why this is smart as hell:**

*   You get the reminder in Slack without needing ChatGPT to integrate with Slack
    
*   You keep your inbox clean
    
*   It works with every recurring reminder you set here in ChatGPT
    

Want me to write the Zapier or Make scenario setup for you next?

## A: 
I get it. You want to keep these sessions tightly aligned with Poppy and ensure they don’t drift into more complex, custom tech builds. Framing these sessions as focused, goal-oriented coworking or strategy sprints is a great approach.

A 3-pack or 4-pack with a clear expiry date (like 60 or 90 days) can create a sense of urgency and commitment. You could frame them as "AI Power Boost Sessions" or "Poppy Power Sprints," emphasizing that these are focused, hands-on sessions to help them overcome roadblocks and level up quickly.

Pricing-wise, you could set them at a rate that reflects the value of your hands-on guidance but keeps it accessible enough for those who are still testing the waters—maybe a bit lower than your full strategy packages but high enough to underscore the premium support.

Position them as a structured, short-term commitment to achieve specific goals with Poppy. They can come with a clear agenda or a set of outcomes, like getting their workflows streamlined or their Poppy setup optimized.

In short, these sessions would be a focused, high-impact offering that provides immediate value and keeps clients on track without veering into more complex territory.

How does that sound for a structure?

## A:

How about we split them into two distinct offers?

First, the "Poppy Power Sprint" could be a single 90-minute strategy and implementation session, priced at around $300. This keeps it accessible for solo entrepreneurs and smaller teams who need that focused boost.

Second, you could introduce a separate "Weekly Cowork Package," which might be shorter, more accountability-focused sessions (e.g., 60 minutes each), sold in a 4-pack for around $800. These sessions would focus on ongoing support and accountability, ensuring clients keep making progress with Poppy without feeling overwhelmed.

This way, you cater to different needs and budgets: the Power Sprint for a deep dive and the Weekly Cowork Package for ongoing support. Both stay aligned with the initial Poppy onboarding and provide clear, structured value.

What do you think about that approach?
